| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979 of<br>14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council with regard to regulatory technical<br>standards on key financial information in the<br>summary of a prospectus, the publication and<br>classification of prospectuses, advertisements for<br>securities, supplements to a prospectus, and the<br>notification portal, and repealing Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) No 382/2014 and<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/301 (OJ<br>L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 1–25). See consolidated<br>version. Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980 of 14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council as regards the format, content,<br>scrutiny and approval of the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004 (OJ L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 26–176). See<br>consolidated version. Commission Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 of 16 December 2020<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 of the<br>European Parliament and of the Council as regards<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division (OJ L 106,<br>26.3.2021, pp. 32–46). RELATED DOCUMENTS<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/337 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 16 February 2021<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>EU Recovery prospectus and targeted adjustments<br>for financial intermediaries and Directive<br>2004/109/EC as regards the use of the single<br>electronic reporting format for annual financial<br>reports, to support the recovery from the COVID-19<br>crisis (OJ L 68, 26.2.2021, pp. 1–13). Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/980 of 14 March 2019, supplementing<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on prospectuses for<br>securities offered to the public or admitted to<br>trading on a regulated market.  It specifies<br>requirements for the format, content, scrutiny,<br>and approval of prospectuses, repealing Commission<br>Regulation (EC) No 809/2004.  The regulation aims<br>to increase transparency and investor protection.<br>**Key aspects covered:**  * **Definitions:**<br>Clarifies terms like "asset-backed securities,"<br>"equivalent third country market," "profit<br>estimate," and "significant gross change."  *<br>**Prospectus Content:**  Details minimum<br>information for various registration documents<br>(equity securities, universal registration<br>document, secondary issuances, closed-end<br>collective investment undertakings, depository<br>receipts, retail/wholesale non-equity securities,<br>asset-backed securities, and securities from<br>third-country issuers).  It also specifies minimum<br>information for securities notes corresponding to<br>these security types.  Additional information is<br>required for prospectuses with complex financial<br>histories, significant financial commitments,<br>securities exchangeable or convertible into<br>shares, securities linked to underlying assets,<br>asset-backed securities, and guarantees.  *<br>**Prospectus Format:**  Specifies the order of<br>information in prospectuses (single or multiple<br>documents), base prospectuses, and final terms.<br>It clarifies the use of "summary" and allows<br>flexibility for universal registration documents<br>and EU Growth prospectuses.  The EU Growth<br>prospectus is designed to reduce the<br>administrative burden for SMEs, with a<br>standardized format and length restrictions on the<br>summary.  * **Scrutiny and Approval:**<br>Establishes criteria for scrutinizing the<br>completeness, comprehensibility, and consistency<br>of prospectuses, allowing for a proportionate<br>approach and additional criteria where necessary<br>for investor protection.  It outlines the process,<br>including document submission (searchable<br>electronic format), iterative review, and lighter<br>scrutiny for similar prospectuses.  It specifies<br>the information to be submitted at different<br>stages of the approval process.  * **EU Growth<br>Prospectus:**  Provides detailed requirements for<br>the EU Growth registration document and securities<br>note for both equity and non-equity securities,<br>including the format and content of the specific<br>summary.  * **Repeal:**  Repeals Commission<br>Regulation (EC) No 809/2004.  * **Entry into<br>force:** The regulation entered into force on the<br>twentieth day following its publication in the<br>Official Journal of the European Union (21.6.2019)<br>and applies from 21 July 2019.   The regulation<br>includes numerous annexes detailing the specific<br>information requirements for each type of<br>prospectus and securities note.  These annexes are<br>too extensive to fully summarize here but cover<br>items such as persons responsible, risk factors,<br>issuer information, financial information, offer<br>terms, and admission to trading. |
| english | Short range devices, RLAN (WiFi), Internet of<br>Things, ultra-wide band (UWB) equipment and<br>Intelligent Transport Systems (ITS) Short range<br>devices, RLAN (WiFi), Internet of Things, equipment<br>Decision 2010/368/EU amending Decision 2006/771/EC<br>on harmonisation of the radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices Decision 2009/381/EC amending<br>Decision 2006/771/EC on harmonisation of the radio<br>spectrum for use by short-range devices Decision<br>2007/90/EC amending Decision 2005/513/EC on the<br>harmonised use of radio spectrum in the 5 GHz<br>frequency band for the implementation of Wireless<br>Access Systems including Radio Local Area Networks<br>(WAS/RLANs) Decision 2008/411/EC on the<br>harmonisation of the 3 400-3 800 MHz frequency<br>band for terrestrial systems capable of providing<br>electronic communications services Decision<br>2005/513/EC on the harmonised use of radio<br>spectrum in the 5 GHz frequency band for the<br>implementation of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy? Council Directive 91/287/EEC of 3 June<br>1991 on the frequency band to be designated for<br>the coordinated introduction of digital European<br>cordless telecommunications (DECT) into the<br>Community (OJ L 144, 8.6.1991, pp. 45-46) RELATED<br>DOCUMENTS              Directive (EU) 2018/1972 of<br>the European Parliament and of the Council of 11<br>December 2018 establishing the European Electronic<br>Communications Code (Recast) (OJ L 321,<br>17.12.2018, pp. 36-214) See consolidated version.<br>Decision No 676/2002/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 7 March 2002on a regulatory<br>framework for radio spectrum policy in the<br>European Community (Radio Spectrum Decision) (OJ L<br>108, 24.4.2002, pp. 1-6) last update 12.11.2020 | This document is Commission Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2019/785 of 14 May 2019, harmonizing radio<br>spectrum use for ultra-wideband (UWB) technology<br>in the European Union.  It repeals Decision<br>2007/131/EC.  The decision aims to create a single<br>market for UWB systems while managing potential<br>interference with existing radio services.  Key<br>aspects include:  * **Definition of UWB<br>equipment:** Equipment using short-range<br>radiocommunication with a frequency range<br>exceeding 50 MHz, potentially overlapping multiple<br>bands. * **Spectrum allocation:** Member States<br>must allocate radio spectrum for UWB equipment<br>within six months, on a non-interference and non-<br>protected basis. This applies indoors, outdoors<br>(excluding fixed installations or antennas), and<br>in motor/railway vehicles, provided the equipment<br>meets specified technical conditions. *<br>**Technical requirements:**  Detailed technical<br>requirements (maximum mean power spectral density<br>(e.i.r.p.), maximum peak power (e.i.r.p.)) are<br>specified in the Annex for various UWB usage<br>types:     * Generic UWB usage.     * Location<br>Tracking Systems Type 1 (LT1).     * UWB devices<br>in motor and railway vehicles (including "trigger-<br>before-transmit" mitigation in 3.8-4.2 GHz and<br>6-8.5 GHz bands).     * UWB onboard aircraft (with<br>specific protection for Fixed Satellite Service<br>and Meteorological Satellite bands).     *<br>Material sensing devices (contact and non-contact<br>based), categorized and with separate limits,<br>including Listen Before Talk (LBT) mechanism<br>requirements in certain bands.  These often have<br>lower power limits than generic UWB and may<br>require duty cycle limitations and/or specific<br>mitigation techniques. * **Mitigation<br>techniques:** The decision allows for alternative<br>mitigation techniques (e.g., those in future<br>harmonized standards) if they provide equivalent<br>spectrum protection.  Specific mitigation<br>techniques like Low Duty Cycle (LDC), Detect and<br>Avoid (DAA), and Transmit Power Control (TPC) are<br>referenced and detailed. * **Monitoring and<br>reporting:** Member States must monitor UWB usage<br>and report findings to the Commission.   The Annex<br>contains extensive tables detailing the specific<br>frequency ranges and power limits for each UWB<br>application type, along with descriptions of<br>required mitigation techniques.  These tables are<br>crucial for understanding the technical<br>requirements of the decision. |
| english | Union registry for emissions trading system<br>allowances Union registry for emissions trading<br>system allowances SUMMARY OF: Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122 on the functioning of the Union<br>registry WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?<br>It aims to guarantee accurate accounting for all<br>allowances issued under the European Union (EU)<br>emissions trading system. KEY POINTS EU registry<br>The EU registry is a single, centralised online<br>database run by the European Commission that holds<br>accounts for operators of facilities such as power<br>stations and airline operators. It covers all<br>countries taking part in the EU greenhouse gas<br>emissions trading scheme (EU ETS), set up by<br>Directive 2003/87/EC, which aims to reduce<br>emissions in a cost-effective manner as part of<br>the EU’s policy to tackle climate change. The<br>registry records: facilities covered by the<br>directive in each EU Member State and any free<br>allowances allocated to those facilities;accounts<br>of companies or individuals with such<br>allowances;transfers of allowances performed by<br>account holders;verified annual CO2 emissions of<br>facilities and airline operators;the annual<br>reconciliation of allowances and verified<br>emissions. Phase IV This regulation sets out the<br>general, operational and maintenance requirements<br>for the EU registry for phase IV of the EU ETS<br>from 2021 to 2030. It replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013 (see summary), which covered phase III<br>(2013–2020) of the EU ETS. Main elements The<br>regulation covers a number of aspects, including<br>the following. The registries system, which is<br>operated and maintained by a central<br>administrator. The regulation introduces a EU<br>transaction log (EUTL), which automatically<br>checks, records and authorises all transactions<br>between accounts in the registry. It replaces the<br>Community independent transaction log from phase<br>II. The status and administration of accounts. The<br>regulation simplifies rules on account management<br>with the aim of reducing the burden on national<br>administrators. Specific rules for the EU ETS<br>registry covering issues such as: verified<br>emissions and compliance;transactions, including<br>rules on the execution of transfers and the<br>creation, allocation and transfer of<br>allowances;improving links between the EU ETS and<br>other ETS schemes where a linking agreement was<br>concluded (e.g. the Swiss ETS – see summary).<br>Technical rules and requirements for the registry<br>and EU transaction log, including national<br>helpdesks for account holders and representatives.<br>Repeal It repeals and replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013. The latter continues to apply until 31<br>December 2025 to all operations in relation to the<br>2013–2020 trading period and to the Kyoto accounts<br>until the true-up (the additional period for the<br>completion of commitments) of the second<br>commitment period of the Kyoto Protocol in 2023.<br>FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLY?<br>It has applied since 1 January 2021. BACKGROUND<br>For further information, see: EU registry<br>(European Commission). MAIN DOCUMENT<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 of<br>12 March 2019 supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>of the European Parliament and of the Council as<br>regards the functioning of the Union Registry (OJ<br>L 177, 2.7.2019, pp. 3–62). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>RELATED DOCUMENTS              Commission<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 of 2 May 2013<br>establishing a Union Registry pursuant to<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council, Decisions No 280/2004/EC and<br>No 406/2009/EC of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council and repealing Commission Regulations<br>(EU) No 920/2010 and No 1193/2011 (OJ L 122,<br>3.5.2013, pp. 1–59). See consolidated version.<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 13 October 2003 establishing<br>a scheme for greenhouse gas emission allowance<br>trading within the Community and amending Council<br>Directive 96/61/EC (OJ L 275, 25.10.2003, pp.<br>32–46). See consolidated version. last update<br>11.01.2022 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122, supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>regarding the functioning of the Union Registry<br>for the EU Emissions Trading System (EU ETS).  It<br>details the rules governing the Union Registry and<br>the European Union Transaction Log (EUTL),<br>effective January 1, 2021, with some exceptions.<br>**Key changes and features of the regulation:**  *<br>**Updated Union Registry:**  The regulation<br>updates the Union Registry's functionality to<br>accommodate the new EU ETS period starting in<br>2021, including amendments from Directive (EU)<br>2018/410.  This includes handling allowances with<br>indicators of their creation period (ten-year<br>intervals starting 2021), restrictions on<br>allowance surrender (only usable for emissions<br>from the first year of their issue), and the<br>removal of international credits (except for<br>completing transactions related to the 2013-2020<br>period).  * **Financial Instrument<br>Classification:** The regulation adapts to the<br>classification of emission allowances as financial<br>instruments under Directive 2014/65/EU, requiring<br>the display of ISIN codes and alignment with<br>financial market legislation.  * **Account<br>Management:**  The regulation details procedures<br>for account opening, updating, and closure for<br>various account types (operator holding accounts,<br>aircraft operator holding accounts, trading<br>accounts, national holding accounts, and ETS<br>management accounts). It emphasizes the need for<br>secure authentication, access rights, and measures<br>against fraud, money laundering, and terrorist<br>financing.  It also specifies the roles and<br>responsibilities of national administrators and<br>the central administrator.  Account status can be<br>"open," "blocked," "closure pending," "closed," or<br>"excluded."  * **Verified Emissions and<br>Compliance:**  The regulation lays out the process<br>for submitting, verifying, and recording verified<br>emissions data for installations and aircraft<br>operators. It defines how compliance status is<br>calculated and the consequences of failing to<br>submit emissions data (account blocking).  *<br>**Transactions:**  The regulation meticulously<br>defines rules for allowance transfers, including<br>execution times and the concept of a "trusted<br>account list" to expedite transactions.  It<br>establishes the fungible and dematerialized nature<br>of allowances, emphasizing the finality of<br>transactions while allowing for reversal of<br>certain processes in specific error cases.  *<br>**Allowance Creation and Allocation:** It covers<br>the creation of allowances, including assigning<br>unique identification codes and ISIN codes, and<br>the transfer of allowances for auctioning and free<br>allocation to stationary installations and<br>aircraft operators.  Specific procedures are<br>detailed for national allocation tables and<br>aviation allocation tables.  * **Linking with<br>Other Systems:** The regulation includes<br>provisions for linking the EU ETS with other<br>emissions trading systems, specifying procedures<br>for transferring allowances between systems and<br>managing the link.  * **Data Protection:**  The<br>regulation addresses data protection and<br>confidentiality, specifying data retention<br>periods, notification procedures for data<br>breaches, and access rights for various<br>authorities.  * **Transitional Provisions:**  It<br>outlines transitional rules for the continued use<br>of accounts and handling of Kyoto units until July<br>1, 2023.  * **Amendments to Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013:**  The regulation amends existing<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013, primarily to<br>incorporate the new provisions and to clarify its<br>continued applicability to operations related to<br>the 2013-2020 trading period.  Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013 is repealed from January 1, 2021, except<br>for operations related to the 2013-2020 period.<br>In essence, Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/1122 provides a comprehensive and detailed<br>framework for the operation of the EU ETS registry<br>system, ensuring its accuracy, security, and<br>compliance with updated legislation. |
| italian | Prospetto da pubblicare per l’offerta pubblica o<br>l’ammissione alla negoziazione di titoli in un<br>mercato regolamentato Prospetto da pubblicare per<br>l’offerta pubblica o l’ammissione alla<br>negoziazione di titoli in un mercato regolamentato<br>SINTESI DI: Regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 relativo al<br>prospetto da pubblicare per l’offerta pubblica o<br>l’ammissione alla negoziazione di titoli in un<br>mercato regolamentato Regolamento delegato (UE)<br>2019/979, che integra il regolamento (UE)<br>2017/1129 per quanto riguarda le norme tecniche di<br>regolamentazione relative alle informazioni<br>finanziarie chiave nella nota di sintesi del<br>prospetto, alla pubblicazione e alla<br>classificazione dei prospetti, alla pubblicità<br>relativa ai titoli, ai supplementi al prospetto e<br>al portale di notifica Regolamento delegato (UE)<br>2019/980 che integra il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129<br>per quanto riguarda il formato, il contenuto, il<br>controllo e l’approvazione del prospetto da<br>pubblicare per l’offerta pubblica o l’ammissione<br>alla negoziazione di titoli in un mercato<br>regolamentato Regolamento delegato (UE) 2021/528<br>che integra il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 per<br>quanto riguarda le informazioni minime contenute<br>nel documento da pubblicare ai fini dell’esenzione<br>dal prospetto in occasione di un’acquisizione<br>mediante offerta pubblica di scambio, una fusione<br>o una scissione QUAL È L’OBIETTIVO DEL<br>REGOLAMENTO? Il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 (il<br>regolamento Prospetto), integrato dai regolamenti<br>delegati (UE) 2019/979, 2019/980 e 2019/528, punta<br>ad aiutare le imprese, comprese le piccole e medie<br>imprese (PMI), ad accedere a differenti forme di<br>finanziamento nell’Unione europea (Unione). Ciò<br>avviene attraverso la semplificazione e<br>l’ottimizzazione delle disposizioni e delle<br>procedure per la redazione l’approvazione e la<br>distribuzione del prospetto* che pubblicano quando<br>emettono titoli* tramite offerta pubblica o<br>ammissione alla negoziazione di titoli in un<br>mercato regolamentato. La legislazione riduce i<br>costi e le formalità per le aziende per consentire<br>agli investitori di assumere la giusta decisione<br>di investimento fornendo informazioni<br>comprensibili, facilmente analizzabili e concise.<br>PUNTI CHIAVE Il regolamento:elimina la necessità<br>del prospetto per tutte le offerte di titoli al<br>pubblico, compresi i progetti in crowdfunding<br>(raccolta di fondi da un gruppo numeroso di<br>persone, spesso tramite internet) inferiori a 1<br>000 000 EUR (il limite precedente era di 100 000<br>EUR); consente agli Stati membri di esentare le<br>offerte di titoli fino a 8 000 000 EUR<br>dall’obbligo di un prospetto, a condizione che non<br>siano subordinate a notifica («passaporto»);<br>stabilisce norme per frenare la tendenza a<br>sovraccaricare i prospetti con fattori di rischio<br>generici; rafforza la convergenza della vigilanza<br>armonizzando il controllo e l’approvazione dei<br>prospetti (comprese le scadenze applicabili) in<br>tutta l’Unione; consente alle società che emettono<br>titoli frequentemente di usufruire del documento<br>di registrazione universale per ottenere<br>l’approvazione in tempi rapidi da parte dei<br>supervisori entro cinque giorni; introduce una<br>banca dati europea online, gestita gratuitamente<br>dall’Autorità europea degli strumenti finanziari e<br>dei mercati (ESMA), contenente tutti i prospetti<br>approvati nello Spazio economico europeo.Il<br>regolamento richiede un prospetto per consentire<br>agli investitori di assumere una decisione<br>informata. Deve contenere:attività, passività,<br>utili, perdite, situazione finanziaria e<br>prospettive dell’emittente e dell’eventuale<br>garante; i diritti connessi ai titoli; i motivi<br>per l’emissione dei titoli e il loro impatto<br>sull’emittente; un riassunto chiaro e accurato di<br>sette pagine (tranne che per l’ammissione alla<br>negoziazione di titoli non azionari destinati solo<br>a investitori qualificati), che<br>contenga:un’introduzione con avvertenze sul<br>rischio che l’investitore possa incorrere in una<br>perdita totale o parziale del capitale<br>investito;informazioni chiave sui titoli, compreso<br>il tipo e la classe dei titoli e i diritti<br>connessi ai titoli;informazioni sull’emittente;una<br>breve descrizione della natura e della portata<br>della garanzia.Il regolamento stabilisce una forma<br>standardizzata e semplificata per un prospetto UE<br>della crescita per:le PMI, definite nella<br>direttiva 2014/65/UE (la direttiva MiFID 2) (si<br>veda la sintesi) come imprese che soddisfano<br>almeno due dei tre criteri seguenti:un numero<br>medio di dipendenti inferiore a 250 durante<br>l’esercizio finanziario;un bilancio totale non<br>superiore a 43 000 000 EUR;un fatturato netto<br>annuale non superiore a 50 000 000 EUR; emittenti<br>diversi dalle PMI, i cui titoli sono o saranno<br>negoziati in un mercato di crescita per le PMI (un<br>mercato che offre accesso ai capitali per le PMI),<br>con una capitalizzazione di borsa media (valore di<br>mercato delle azioni della società) inferiore a<br>500 000 000 EUR; offerenti di titoli emessi da<br>emittenti di cui ai due punti precedenti; società<br>non quotate (non quotate in nessuna borsa) che<br>offrano titoli al pubblico che non superino i 20<br>000 000 EUR, calcolati su un periodo di 12 mesi, e<br>a condizione che abbiano meno di 500 dipendenti;<br>emittenti, diversi dalle PMI, che offrano azioni<br>al pubblico e allo stesso tempo chiedano<br>l’ammissione di tali azioni alla negoziazione su<br>un mercato di crescita per le PMI, a condizione<br>che:tali emittenti non abbiano azioni già ammesse<br>alla negoziazione su un mercato di crescita per le<br>PMI;il valore combinato del prezzo finale<br>dell’offerta (o, se non disponibile, il prezzo<br>massimo) e il numero totale di azioni in<br>circolazione immediatamente dopo l’offerta al<br>pubblico di azioni sia inferiore a 200 000 000<br>EUR.Le società sopracitate possono beneficiare del<br>prospetto su misura purché non abbiano titoli<br>ammessi alla negoziazione in un mercato<br>regolamentato. Il regolamento fornisce un<br>prospetto semplificato per le società quotate da<br>almeno 18 mesi in un mercato regolamentato o in un<br>mercato di crescita per le PMI e che intendano<br>emettere azioni aggiuntive o aumentare il debito<br>(emissioni secondarie). Il regolamento armonizza<br>le informazioni minime contenute nel documento da<br>pubblicare ai fini dell’esenzione dal prospetto in<br>occasione di un’acquisizione mediante offerta<br>pubblica di scambio, una fusione o una scissione.<br>Regolamenti di modificaIl regolamento (UE)<br>2019/2115 è volto a promuovere l’uso dei mercati<br>di crescita per le PMI riducendo le formalità e<br>gli oneri amministrativi a carico delle PMI in<br>termini di obblighi di informazione e di un<br>prospetto semplificato. Il regolamento (UE)<br>2020/1503 introduce un’esenzione dal prospetto per<br>le offerte di titoli al pubblico presentate da<br>fornitori di servizi di crowdfunding che non<br>superino la soglia di 5 000 000 EUR in conformità<br>con le condizioni specificate in tale regolamento.<br>Il regolamento (UE) 2021/337 introduce un nuovo<br>«prospetto UE della ripresa» per sostenere la<br>ripresa delle imprese dalla crisi COVID-19. Questo<br>prospetto abbreviato, di una lunghezza massima di<br>30 facciate più un riassunto di due pagine,<br>semplifica alle imprese l’operazione di raccolta<br>dei capitali per soddisfare le proprie esigenze di<br>finanziamento, garantendo al contempo un’adeguata<br>informazione agli investitori. Il prospetto della<br>ripresa sarà disponibile per gli aumenti di<br>capitale non superiori al 150 % del capitale in<br>essere entro un periodo di 12 mesi e si applica<br>fino alla fine del 2022.Atti delegati La<br>Commissione europea ha adottato i seguenti atti.Il<br>regolamento delegato (UE) 2019/980 che fissa i<br>dettagli del preciso contenuto e formato del<br>prospetto, così come il controllo e l’approvazione<br>dello stesso. Il regolamento (UE) 2019/979 che<br>fissa i dettagli relativi alle informazioni<br>finanziarie chiave nella nota di sintesi del<br>prospetto, alla pubblicazione e alla<br>classificazione dei prospetti, alla pubblicità<br>relativa ai titoli e ai supplementi relativi allo<br>stesso. Il regolamento delegato (UE) 2020/1273 che<br>modifica e corregge il regolamento delegato (UE)<br>2019/980. Il regolamento delegato (UE) 2020/1272<br>che modifica e corregge il regolamento delegato<br>(UE) 2019/979. Il regolamento delegato (UE)<br>2021/528 che stabilisce le informazioni minime<br>contenute nel documento da pubblicare ai fini<br>dell’esenzione dal prospetto in occasione di<br>un’acquisizione mediante offerta pubblica di<br>scambio, una fusione o una scissione.Relazione La<br>Commissione dovrà presentare una relazione<br>sull’applicazione della legislazione entro il 21<br>luglio 2022. A PARTIRE DA QUANDO SI APPLICANO I<br>REGOLAMENTI? Il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 e i<br>regolamenti delegati (UE) 2019/979 e (EU) 2019/980<br>sono in vigore dal 21 luglio 2019. Il regolamento<br>delegato (UE) n. 2021/528 è in vigore dal 15<br>aprile 2021. CONTESTO La direttiva 2003/71/CE<br>aveva il fine di semplificare la raccolta di<br>capitali per le aziende in tutta l’Unione sulla<br>base dell’approvazione da parte di un unico<br>supervisore nazionale. Ciò dava un «passaporto» ai<br>prospetti che contenevano offerte<br>transfrontaliere. Il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129,<br>che abroga e sostituisce la direttiva 2003/71/CEE,<br>affronta le aree di incertezza giuridica e gli<br>oneri amministrativi ingiustificati che erano<br>emersi nel tempo. È considerato una pietra miliare<br>fondamentale verso l’unione dei mercati europei<br>dei capitali.Per ulteriori informazioni, si<br>veda:Prospetto titoli (Commissione europea).<br>Prospetto (Autorità europea degli strumenti<br>finanziari e dei mercati). TERMINI CHIAVE<br>Prospetto. Un documento giuridico che descrive<br>l’area di attività di un’azienda, le sue finanze e<br>la compagine societaria. I potenziali investitori<br>lo usano per decidere se acquistare o meno i<br>titoli offerti da un’azienda. Titoli. Azioni,<br>obbligazioni e derivati. DOCUMENTI PRINCIPALI<br>Regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 del Parlamento europeo<br>e del Consiglio, del 14 giugno 2017, relativo al<br>prospetto da pubblicare per l’offerta pubblica o<br>l’ammissione alla negoziazione di titoli in un<br>mercato regolamentato, e che abroga la direttiva<br>2003/71/CE (GU L 168, del 30.6.2017, pag. 12). Le<br>modifiche successive al regolamento (UE) 2017/1129<br>sono state integrate nel testo originale. La<br>versione consolidata ha esclusivamente valore<br>documentale. Regolamento delegato (UE) 2019/979<br>della Commissione, del 14 marzo 2019, che integra<br>il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 del Parlamento<br>europeo e del Consiglio per quanto riguarda le<br>norme tecniche di regolamentazione relative alle<br>informazioni finanziarie chiave nella nota di<br>sintesi del prospetto, alla pubblicazione e alla<br>classificazione dei prospetti, alla pubblicità<br>relativa ai titoli, ai supplementi al prospetto e<br>al portale di notifica, e che abroga i regolamenti<br>delegati (UE) n. 382/2014 e (UE) 2016/301 della<br>Commissione (GU L 166 del 21.6.2019, pag. 1). Si<br>veda la versione consolidata. Regolamento delegato<br>(UE) 2019/980 della Commissione, del 14 marzo<br>2019, che integra il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129<br>del Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio per quanto<br>riguarda il formato, il contenuto, il controllo e<br>l’approvazione del prospetto da pubblicare per<br>l’offerta pubblica o l’ammissione alla<br>negoziazione di titoli in un mercato<br>regolamentato, e che abroga il regolamento (CE) n.<br>809/2004 della Commissione (GU L 166 del<br>21.6.2019, pag. 26). Si veda la versione<br>consolidata. Regolamento delegato (UE) 2021/528<br>della Commissione, del 16 dicembre 2020, che<br>integra il regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 del<br>Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio per quanto<br>riguarda le informazioni minime contenute nel<br>documento da pubblicare ai fini dell’esenzione dal<br>prospetto in occasione di un’acquisizione mediante<br>offerta pubblica di scambio, una fusione o una<br>scissione (GU L 106 del 26.3.2021, pag. 32).<br>DOCUMENTI CORRELATI Regolamento (UE) 2021/337 del<br>Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio, del 16<br>febbraio 2021 che modifica il regolamento (UE)<br>2017/1129 per quanto riguarda il prospetto UE<br>della ripresa e adeguamenti mirati per gli<br>intermediari finanziari, nonché la direttiva<br>2004/109/CE per quanto riguarda l’uso del formato<br>elettronico unico di comunicazione per le<br>relazioni finanziarie annuali, per sostenere la<br>ripresa dalla crisi COVID-19 (GU L 68 del<br>26.2.2021, pag. 1). Regolamento (UE) 2020/1503 del<br>Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio, del 7 ottobre<br>2020, relativo ai fornitori europei di servizi di<br>crowdfunding per le imprese, e che modifica il<br>regolamento (UE) 2017/1129 e la direttiva (UE)<br>2019/1937 (GU L 347 del 20.10.2020, pag. 1).<br>Regolamento (UE) n. 2019/2115 del Parlamento<br>europeo e del Consiglio, del 27 novembre 2019, che<br>modifica la direttiva 2014/65/UE e i regolamenti<br>(UE) n. 596/2014 e (UE) 2017/1129 per quanto<br>riguarda la promozione dell’uso dei mercati di<br>crescita per le PMI (GU L 320 dell’11.12.2019,<br>pag. 1). Ultimo aggiornamento: 22.11.2021 | This is a very long text, the Delegate Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/980 of the European Commission, dated<br>March 14, 2019, and published June 21, 2019.  It<br>details the format, content, review, and approval<br>process for prospectuses related to public<br>offerings or admission of securities to trading on<br>a regulated market within the EU.  The regulation<br>aims to increase investor protection and<br>transparency while streamlining the prospectus<br>process, particularly for SMEs.  **Key aspects of<br>the regulation include:**  * **Harmonization of<br>Prospectus Requirements:** The regulation aims to<br>establish a single set of rules for the format,<br>content, review, and approval of prospectuses,<br>replacing Commission Regulation (EC) No 809/2004.<br>* **Flexibility and Proportionality:**  While<br>setting minimum information requirements, the<br>regulation allows for flexibility depending on<br>factors like the type of issuer, security,<br>offering, and whether there's admission to<br>trading.  A more proportionate approach is allowed<br>for specialized issuers (e.g., real estate<br>companies) and simplified requirements for<br>secondary offerings and SMEs (using the EU Growth<br>Prospectus).  * **Specific Information<br>Requirements:**  The regulation provides detailed<br>requirements for various types of issuers and<br>securities including:     * Equity securities<br>* Universal registration document     * Secondary<br>offerings of equity and non-equity securities<br>* Closed-end investment funds     * Depository<br>receipts     * Non-equity securities for retail<br>and wholesale investors     * Non-equity<br>securities issued by third-country entities     *<br>Securitized debt  * **Prospectus Structure:**  The<br>regulation specifies the order of information in a<br>prospectus, including the sections for summary,<br>risk factors, and other required information.<br>However, it allows some flexibility, especially<br>for universal registration documents.  The EU<br>Growth Prospectus has a more fixed structure to<br>reduce the administrative burden for SMEs.  *<br>**Base Prospectus and Final Terms:**  The<br>regulation distinguishes between information to be<br>included in the base prospectus, information that<br>can be left blank and detailed later in the final<br>terms, and information exclusive to the final<br>terms.  * **Review and Approval Process:** The<br>regulation outlines a detailed iterative review<br>process for prospectuses by competent authorities.<br>This includes specifying the documents and formats<br>to be submitted (searchable electronic format is<br>required), handling of amendments, and the<br>criteria for reviewing the completeness,<br>comprehensibility, and consistency of information.<br>Lighter review is permitted for prospectuses<br>substantially similar to previously approved ones.<br>* **EU Growth Prospectus:**  This simplified<br>prospectus is designed to reduce administrative<br>burden for SMEs, with a specific standardized<br>format and reduced content. A specific summary is<br>required.  * **Abrogation:** Commission Regulation<br>(EC) No 809/2004 is repealed.  * **Effective<br>Date:** The regulation was applicable from July<br>21, 2019.   The regulation includes numerous<br>annexes detailing the specific information<br>requirements for each type of prospectus and<br>document.  The complete text is highly technical<br>and legally binding within the EU. |

di<br>fornire servizi di comunicazioni elettroniche<br>Decisione 2005/513/CE sull’uso armonizzato dello<br>spettro radio nella banda di frequenze 5 GHz per<br>l’implementazione di sistemi di accesso senza<br>fili, comprese le reti locali in radiofrequenza<br>(WAS/RLAN) Direttiva 91/287/CEE sulla banda di<br>frequenza da designare per l’introduzione<br>coordinata nella Comunità di un sistema digitale<br>di telecomunicazione senza filo (DECT) QUALI SONO<br>GLI SCOPI DELLA DIRETTIVA E DELLE DECISIONI? Le<br>decisioni di esecuzione riguardano principalmente<br>l’armonizzazione, mentre altre riguardano<br>specifiche bande di frequenza per scopi specifici,<br>oltre ai limiti sulla potenza del segnale e alle<br>interferenze dannose ove applicabile. Gli Stati<br>membri sono responsabili della gestione dello<br>spettro radio e le modifiche riflettono<br>l’evoluzione dell’armonizzazione e degli accordi<br>tecnici europei e internazionali. La direttiva<br>«DECT» assegna la banda di frequenza 1 880-1 900<br>MHz per le comunicazioni digitali senza fili entro<br>il 1o gennaio 1992 e obbliga gli Stati membri ad<br>applicare le leggi, i regolamenti e le<br>disposizioni amministrative nazionali necessarie.<br>PUNTI CHIAVE Le decisioni Le decisioni di<br>esecuzione riguardano i dispositivi radio gestiti<br>mediante autorizzazione generale o senza licenza o<br>condivisi dagli utenti finali. Ciò comprende i<br>dispositivi di rete ad accesso locale in<br>radiofrequenza (WiFi) che hanno mostrato una forte<br>crescita della domanda dello spettro radio, come<br>riconosciuto dal Codice europeo delle<br>comunicazioni elettroniche del 2018. Molti di<br>questi atti sono decisioni di armonizzazione.<br>Altri riguardano le bande di frequenza per scopi<br>diversi, ad esempio un’enorme varietà di<br>dispositivi a corto raggio, apparecchiature di<br>Internet degli oggetti, apparecchiature a banda<br>ultra larga, allarmi, apriporta, impianti medici,<br>sistemi di trasporto intelligenti, dispositivi di<br>identificazione a radiofrequenza ( RFID),<br>radiodeterminazione, sondaggio del suolo e nuovi<br>tipi di dispositivi da macchina a macchina, nonché<br>apparecchiature per la realizzazione di programmi<br>ed eventi speciali (PMSE) come collegamenti video<br>senza fili o microfoni e telefoni digitali senza<br>fili. Un’ulteriore banda con autorizzazione<br>generale riguarda la sicurezza dei veicoli, in<br>particolare il funzionamento dei sistemi di<br>trasporto intelligenti (ITS). Le varie decisioni<br>di esecuzione riguardano i seguenti spettri radio,<br>oltre ai limiti sulla potenza del segnale e alle<br>interferenze dannose ove applicabili:banda di<br>frequenza 5 GHz (5 150-5 350 MHz e 5 470-5 725<br>MHz) per i sistemi di accesso senza fili, comprese<br>le reti locali in radiofrequenza (WAS / RLAN -<br>banda larga WiFi); banda di frequenza 3 400-3 800<br>MHz per i sistemi terrestri per «reti di<br>comunicazione elettronica fisse, portatili e<br>mobili»; banda di frequenze 5 875-5 935 MHz  per<br>applicazioni legate alla sicurezza dei sistemi di<br>trasporto intelligenti; spettro radio per<br>l’utilizzo da parte di apparecchiature a corto<br>raggio; banda di spettro radio 24 GHz ai fini<br>dell’uso limitato nel tempo di apparecchiature<br>radar a corto raggio per autoveicoli; utilizzo<br>dello spettro radio da parte delle apparecchiature<br>audio senza fili per la realizzazione di programmi<br>e di eventi speciali; banda di frequenza 2 010-2<br>025 MHz per collegamenti video senza fili<br>portatili o mobili e videocamere senza fili per la<br>realizzazione di programmi ed eventi speciali;<br>bande di frequenze 900 MHz e 1 800 MHz per i<br>sistemi terrestri in grado di fornire servizi di<br>comunicazioni elettroniche in relazione<br>all’Internet degli oggetti; spettro radio per<br>l’utilizzo di apparecchiature a corto raggio nelle<br>bande di frequenza 874-876 MHz e 915-921 MHz;<br>spettro radio per apparecchiature che utilizzano<br>la tecnologia a banda ultra larga, ad esempio per<br>il rilevamento della posizione di veicoli e<br>aeromobili.Direttiva 91/287/CEE La direttiva<br>impone agli Stati membri di assegnare la banda di<br>frequenze 1 880-1 900 MHz alle comunicazioni<br>digitali senza fili entro il 1o gennaio 1992.
