(Commissione europea)<br>Armonizzazione dello spettro radio per dispositivi<br>a corto raggio (Commissione europea) Nuove<br>disposizioni sulle telecomunicazioni nell’UE:<br>migliorare la connettività e proteggere meglio gli<br>utenti (Commissione europea) L’Internet degli<br>oggetti (Commissione europea). DOCUMENTI<br>PRINCIPALI Decisione di esecuzione (UE) 2020/1426<br>della Commissione del 7 ottobre 2020 relativa<br>all’uso armonizzato dello spettro radio nella<br>banda di frequenze 5 875-5 935 MHz per le<br>applicazioni legate alla sicurezza dei sistemi di<br>trasporto intelligenti (ITS) e che abroga la<br>decisione 2008/671/CE (GU L 328 del 9.10.2020,<br>pag. 19). Decisione di esecuzione (UE) 2019/785<br>della Commissione, del 14 maggio 2019, relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio per le<br>apparecchiature che utilizzano la tecnologia a<br>banda ultralarga nell’Unione, e che abroga la<br>decisione 2007/131/CE (GU L 127 del 16.5.2019,<br>pag. 23). Decisione di esecuzione (UE) 2018/1538<br>della Commissione, dell’11 ottobre 2018, relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio per<br>l’utilizzo di apparecchiature a corto raggio nelle<br>bande di frequenza 874-876 MHz e 915-921 MHz (GU L<br>257 del 15.10.2018, pag. 57). Decisione di<br>esecuzione (UE) 2018/637 della Commissione, del 20<br>aprile 2018, che modifica la decisione 2009/766/CE<br>della Commissione relativa all’armonizzazione<br>delle bande di frequenze 900 MHz e 1 800 MHz per i<br>sistemi terrestri in grado di fornire servizi di<br>comunicazioni elettroniche paneuropee nella<br>Comunità per quanto riguarda le condizioni<br>tecniche per l’Internet delle cose (GU L 105 del<br>25.4.2018, pag. 27). Decisione di esecuzione (UE)<br>2017/2077 della Commissione, del 10 novembre 2017,<br>sulla modifica della decisione 2005/50/CE relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio nella banda<br>di frequenze 24 GHz ai fini dell’uso limitato nel<br>tempo di apparecchiature radar a corto raggio per<br>autoveicoli nella Comunità (GU L 295 del<br>14.11.2017, pag. 75). Decisione di esecuzione (UE)<br>2017/1483 della Commissione, dell’8 agosto 2017,<br>recante modifica della decisione 2006/771/CE<br>relativa all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio<br>per l’utilizzo da parte di apparecchiature a corto<br>raggio e che abroga la decisione 2006/804/CE (GU L<br>214 del 18.8.2017, pag. 3). Decisione di<br>esecuzione (UE)2016/339 della Commissione, dell’8<br>marzo 2016, relativa all’armonizzazione della<br>banda di frequenza 2 010-2 025 MHz per<br>collegamenti video senza fili portatili o mobili e<br>videocamere senza fili per la realizzazione di<br>programmi ed eventi speciali (GU L 63 del<br>10.3.2016, pag. 5). Decisione di esecuzione<br>2014/641/UE della Commissione, del 1o settembre<br>2014, relativa alle condizioni tecniche<br>armonizzate per l’utilizzo dello spettro radio da<br>parte delle apparecchiature audio senza fili per<br>la realizzazione di programmi e di eventi speciali<br>nell’Unione (GU L 263 del 3.9.2014, pag. 29).<br>Decisione di esecuzione 2013/752/UE della<br>Commissione, dell’11 dicembre 2013, recante<br>modifica della decisione 2006/771/CE relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio per<br>l’utilizzo da parte di apparecchiature a corto<br>raggio e che abroga la decisione 2005/928/CE (GU L<br>334 del 13.12.2013, pag. 17). Decisione di<br>esecuzione 2011/829/UE della Commissione, dell’8<br>dicembre 2011, recante modifica della decisione<br>2006/771/CE relativa all’armonizzazione dello<br>spettro radio per l’utilizzo da parte di<br>apparecchiature a corto raggio (GU L 329 del<br>13.12.2011, pag. 10). Decisione di esecuzione (UE)<br>2011/485/UE della Commissione, del 29 luglio 2011,<br>sulla modifica della decisione 2005/50/CE relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio nella banda<br>di frequenze 24 GHz ai fini dell’uso limitato nel<br>tempo di apparecchiature radar a corto raggio per<br>autoveicoli nella Comunità (GU L 198 del<br>30.7.2011, pag. 71). Decisione 2010/368/UE della<br>Commissione, del 30 giugno 2010, recante modifica<br>della decisione 2006/771/CE relativa<br>all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio per<br>l’utilizzo da parte di apparecchiature a corto<br>raggio (GU L 166 del 1.7.2010, pag. 33). Decisione<br>2009/381/CE della Commissione, del 13 maggio 2009,<br>recante modifica della decisione 2006/771/CE<br>relativa all’armonizzazione dello spettro radio<br>per l’utilizzo da parte di apparecchiature a corto<br>raggio (GU L 119 del 14.5.2009, pag. 32).<br>Decisione 2007/90/CE della Commissione, del 12<br>febbraio 2007 ,recante modifica della decisione<br>2005/513/CE sull’uso armonizzato dello spettro<br>radio nella banda di frequenze 5 GHz per<br>l’implementazione di sistemi di accesso senza<br>fili, comprese le reti locali in radiofrequenza<br>(WAS/RLAN) (GU L 41 del 13.2.2007, pag. 10).<br>Decisione 2008/411/CE della Commissione, del 21<br>maggio 2008, relativa all’armonizzazione della<br>banda di frequenze 3 400-3 800 MHz per i sistemi<br>terrestri in grado di fornire servizi di<br>comunicazioni elettroniche nella Comunità (GU L<br>144 del 4.6.2008, pag. 77). Le successive<br>modifiche alla decisione 2008/411/UE sono state<br>incorporate nel documento originale. La versione<br>consolidata ha esclusivamente valore documentale.<br>Decisione 2005/513/CE della Commissione, dell’11<br>luglio 2005, sull’uso armonizzato dello spettro<br>radio nella banda di frequenze 5 GHz per<br>l’implementazione di sistemi di accesso senza fili<br>comprese le reti locali in radiofrequenza<br>(WAS/RLAN) (GU L 187 del 19.7.2005, pag. 22). Si<br>veda la versione consolidata. Direttiva 91/287/CEE<br>del Consiglio, del 3 giugno 1991, sulla banda di<br>frequenza da assegnare per l’introduzione<br>coordinata nella Comunità di un sistema digitale<br>di telecomunicazione senza filo (DECT) (GU L 144<br>dell’8.6.1991, pag. 45). DOCUMENTI CORRELATI<br>Direttiva (UE) 2018/1972 del Parlamento europeo e<br>del Consiglio, dell’11 dicembre 2018, che<br>istituisce il codice europeo delle comunicazioni<br>elettroniche (rifusione) (GU L 321 del 17.12.2018,<br>pag. 36). Si veda la versione consolidata.<br>Decisione n. 676/2002/CE del Parlamento europeo e<br>del Consiglio, del 7 marzo 2002, relativa a un<br>quadro normativo per la politica in materia di<br>spettro radio nella Comunità europea (Decisione<br>spettro radio) (GU L 108 del 24.4.2002, pag. 1).<br>Ultimo aggiornamento: 12.11.2020 | Questa decisione di esecuzione della Commissione<br>europea (UE) 2019/785, del 14 maggio 2019,<br>armonizza le condizioni tecniche per l'uso dello<br>spettro radio da parte di apparecchiature Ultra-<br>Wideband (UWB) nell'Unione Europea, abrogando la<br>decisione 2007/131/CE.  L'obiettivo è garantire la<br>disponibilità di spettro armonizzato in tutta<br>l'UE, rimuovendo gli ostacoli all'adozione della<br>tecnologia UWB e creando un mercato unico.  Il<br>documento riconosce il potenziale di interferenza,<br>anche con servizi di radioastronomia, esplorazione<br>terrestre via satellite e ricerca spaziale, e<br>stabilisce limiti e tecniche di mitigazione per<br>prevenire interferenze dannose, bilanciando gli<br>interessi dei servizi esistenti con l'introduzione<br>di nuove tecnologie.  Si basa su una relazione<br>della Conferenza europea delle amministrazioni<br>delle poste e delle telecomunicazioni (CEPT).<br>**Definizioni chiave:**  Il testo definisce<br>"apparecchiatura UWB", "su base di non<br>interferenza e senza diritto a protezione", "in<br>ambienti chiusi", "veicolo a motore", "veicolo<br>ferroviario", "e.i.r.p.", "densità spettrale di<br>potenza media", "potenza di picco", "densità<br>spettrale di potenza totale", "a bordo di<br>aeromobili" e "LT1" (sistemi di localizzazione).<br>**Condizioni tecniche:** L'allegato specifica i<br>limiti tecnici per la densità spettrale di potenza<br>media e la potenza di picco per diverse gamme di<br>frequenza, suddivisi per:  * **Uso generico UWB:**<br>Definisce limiti per diverse bande di frequenza,<br>con opzioni per tecniche di mitigazione come LDC<br>(Low Duty Cycle) e DAA (Detect and Avoid). *<br>**Sistemi di geolocalizzazione LT1:** Limiti<br>simili all'uso generico, ma specifici per i<br>sistemi di localizzazione. * **Dispositivi UWB su<br>veicoli a motore e ferroviari:** Limiti specifici,<br>con opzioni per LDC, DAA e TPC (Transmit Power<br>Control), e un limite esterno.  Include requisiti<br>per il trigger-before-transmit nei sistemi di<br>accesso veicolare nelle bande 3,8-4,2 GHz e 6-8,5<br>GHz. * **Dispositivi UWB a bordo di aeromobili:**<br>Limiti specifici per diverse bande di frequenza,<br>con alcune protezioni aggiuntive per servizi<br>satellitari. * **Dispositivi di rilevamento di<br>materiali UWB:**  Suddivisi in dispositivi a<br>contatto e senza contatto, con limiti specifici<br>per entrambe le categorie e diverse bande di<br>frequenza. Include l'uso di LBT (Listen Before<br>Talk) e la protezione di specifici servizi radio.<br>**Obblighi degli Stati membri:** Gli Stati membri<br>devono designare e rendere disponibile lo spettro<br>per le apparecchiature UWB entro sei mesi<br>dall'entrata in vigore della decisione, a<br>condizione che rispettino le condizioni tecniche<br>dell'allegato e siano utilizzati in ambienti<br>chiusi o, all'aperto, non siano collegati a<br>installazioni fisse.  Devono anche monitorare<br>l'uso dello spettro e riferire alla Commissione.<br>In sintesi, la decisione mira ad armonizzare l'uso<br>della tecnologia UWB nell'UE, stabilendo limiti e<br>tecniche di mitigazione per garantire la<br>coesistenza con altri servizi radio, promuovendo<br>al contempo l'innovazione.  L'uso di tecniche di<br>mitigazione alternative è consentito se<br>garantiscono un livello di protezione dello<br>spettro almeno equivalente. |
| italian | Registro dell’Unione per il sistema di scambio di<br>quote di emissioni Registro dell’Unione per il<br>sistema di scambio di quote di emissioni   SINTESI<br>DI: Regolamento delegato (UE) 2019/1122 per quanto<br>riguarda il funzionamento del registro dell’Unione<br>QUAL È L’OBIETTIVO DEL REGOLAMENTO? Mira a<br>garantire l’accurata contabilizzazione delle quote<br>rilasciate nell’ambito del sistema di scambio di<br>quote di emissioni dell’Unione europea (Unione).<br>PUNTI CHIAVE Registro dell’UnioneIl registro<br>dell’Unione è una banca dati online centralizzata<br>e unica gestita dall’Unione europea sui conti<br>degli operatori che gestiscono impianti quali<br>centrali elettriche e linee aeree. Copre tutti i<br>paesi che partecipano al sistema di scambio di<br>quote di emissioni di gas a effetto serra<br>dell’Unione (EU ETS), istituito dalla direttiva<br>2003/87/CE, che mira a ridurre le emissioni in<br>modo economicamente vantaggioso nell’ambito della<br>politica dell’Unione per affrontare il cambiamento<br>climatico. Il registro riguarda:gli impianti<br>coperti dalla direttiva in ciascuno Stato membro<br>dell’Unione e le eventuali quote gratuite<br>assegnate a tali impianti;i conti delle società o<br>delle persone titolari di tali quote;i<br>trasferimenti di quote eseguiti da titolari di<br>conti;i dati annuali verificati sulle emissioni di<br>CO2 degli impianti e degli operatori di linee<br>aeree;La concordanza annuale delle quote e delle<br>emissioni verificate.Fase IVIl regolamento<br>stabilisce i requisiti generali, operativi e di<br>manutenzione per il registro UE per la fase IV<br>dell’EU ETS dal 2021 al 2030. Sostituisce il<br>regolamento (UE) n. 389/2013 (si veda la sintesi),<br>che riguardava la fase III (2013–2020) di EU<br>ETS.Elementi principali Il regolamento riguarda<br>una serie di aspetti, tra cui i seguenti.Il<br>sistema dei registri, che viene gestito e tenuto<br>da un amministratore centrale. Il regolamento<br>introduce un catalogo delle operazioni dell’Unione<br>europea (EUTL) che verifica, registra e autorizza<br>le operazioni tra i conti presenti nel registro.<br>Sostituisce il catalogo indipendente delle<br>operazioni della Comunità dalla fase II. Stato e<br>amministrazione dei conti Il regolamento<br>semplifica le regole sulla gestione dei conti con<br>lo scopo di ridurre gli oneri per gli<br>amministratori nazionali. Contiene regole<br>specifiche  per il registro EU ETS che riguardano<br>questioni quali:emissioni verificate e<br>conformità;operazioni, comprese le regole<br>sull’esecuzione dei trasferimenti e sulla<br>creazione, l’assegnazione e il trasferimento di<br>quote;miglioramento dei collegamenti tra EU ETS e<br>altri sistemi ETS ove siano stati conclusi accordi<br>di collegamento (ad es. l’ETS svizzero - si veda<br>la sintesi). Disposizioni tecniche e requisiti per<br>il registro e il catalogo delle operazioni<br>dell’Unione europea, compresi i punti di<br>assistenza nazionali per i titolari e ai<br>rappresentanti dei conti.Abrogazione Abroga e<br>sostituisce il regolamento (UE) n. 389/2013.<br>Quest’ultimo rimane in vigore fino al 31 dicembre<br>2025 per tutte le transazioni necessarie in<br>relazione al periodo di scambio compreso tra il<br>2013 e il 2020 e ai conti di Kyoto fino al periodo<br>di adempimento degli impegni (periodo di<br>allineamento) del secondo periodo di impegno del<br>Protocollo di Kyoto nel 2023. A PARTIRE DA QUANDO<br>SI APPLICA IL REGOLAMENTO? Il regolamento è in<br>vigore dall’1 gennaio 2021. CONTESTO Per ulteriori<br>informazioni, si veda:Registro dell’Unione<br>(Commissione europea). DOCUMENTO PRINCIPALE<br>Regolamento delegato (UE) 2019/1122 della<br>Commissione, del 12 marzo 2019, che integra la<br>direttiva 2003/87/CE del Parlamento europeo e del<br>Consiglio per quanto riguarda il funzionamento del<br>registro dell’Unione (GU L 177 del 2.7.2019, pag.<br>3). Le modifiche successive al regolamento (UE)<br>2019/1122 sono state integrate nel testo<br>originale. La versione consolidata ha<br>esclusivamente valore documentale. DOCUMENTI<br>CORRELATI Regolamento (UE) n. 389/2013 della<br>Commissione, del 2 maggio 2013, che istituisce un<br>registro dell’Unione conformemente alla direttiva<br>2003/87/CE del Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio,<br>alle decisioni n. 280/2004/CE e n. 406/2009/CE del<br>Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio e che abroga i<br>regolamenti (UE) n. 920/2010 e n. 1193/2011 della<br>Commissione (GU L 122 del 3.5.2013, pag. 1). Si<br>veda la versione consolidata. Direttiva 2003/87/CE<br>del Parlamento europeo e del Consiglio, del 13<br>ottobre 2003, che istituisce un sistema per lo<br>scambio di quote di emissioni dei gas a effetto<br>serra nella Comunità e che modifica la Direttiva<br>96/61/CE del Consiglio (GU L 275 del 25.10.2003,<br>pag. 32). Si veda la versione consolidata. Ultimo<br>aggiornamento: 11.01.2022 | Questo documento è il Regolamento Delegato (UE)<br>2019/1122 della Commissione del 12 marzo 2019, che<br>integra la direttiva 2003/87/CE per quanto<br>riguarda il funzionamento del registro dell'Unione<br>del sistema di scambio di quote di emissioni<br>dell'Unione europea (EU ETS).  Il regolamento si<br>applica alle quote create per l'EU ETS e definisce<br>termini chiave come "amministratore centrale",<br>"amministratore nazionale" e "titolare del conto".<br>**Obiettivi principali del regolamento:**  *<br>**Aggiornamento del registro dell'Unione:** Il<br>regolamento aggiorna il registro dell'Unione per<br>allinearlo alle modifiche della direttiva<br>2003/87/CE (in particolare la direttiva (UE)<br>2018/410), inclusi i nuovi periodi di scambio e la<br>classificazione delle quote di emissioni come<br>strumenti finanziari.  Questo include la<br>tracciatura del periodo di emissione delle quote a<br>partire dal 2021. * **Gestione delle quote:** Il<br>regolamento definisce regole chiare per la<br>creazione, il trasferimento, la restituzione e la<br>soppressione delle quote, incluso il trattamento<br>delle quote in eccesso e la prevenzione di usi<br>impropri. * **Gestione dei conti:** Definisce i<br>tipi di conti (gestione ETS, deposito ETS, scambio<br>ETS), le procedure per l'apertura, la chiusura e<br>la sospensione degli accessi, l'assegnazione dei<br>rappresentanti autorizzati, e le procedure per<br>l'aggiornamento delle informazioni.  Include<br>disposizioni dettagliate sulla verifica delle<br>informazioni fornite dai titolari dei conti e dai<br>verificatori per prevenire frodi e riciclaggio. *<br>**Interazione con le autorità:** Descrive<br>l'interazione tra amministratori nazionali,<br>amministratore centrale e autorità competenti per<br>quanto riguarda l'assegnazione gratuita delle<br>quote, la gestione dei dati sulle emissioni e la<br>chiusura dei conti. Include la segnalazione di<br>quote in eccesso e la gestione delle quote<br>rilasciate a Stati membri che hanno avviato la<br>procedura di recesso dall'UE. * **Collegamenti con<br>altri sistemi:** Il regolamento affronta<br>l'integrazione dell'EU ETS con altri sistemi di<br>scambio di quote di emissioni, definendo le<br>procedure per il collegamento e la sospensione<br>dello stesso. * **Aspetti tecnici e di<br>sicurezza:**  Il regolamento delinea i requisiti<br>tecnici del registro dell'Unione e del catalogo<br>delle operazioni dell'Unione europea (EUTL),<br>inclusa la sicurezza, l'autenticazione, la<br>disponibilità, la gestione delle modifiche e la<br>cooperazione con le autorità di contrasto per la<br>prevenzione di frodi e attività criminali. *<br>**Trattamento dei dati:**  Definisce le<br>responsabilità in materia di trattamento dei dati<br>personali e stabilisce procedure chiare per la<br>conservazione e la cancellazione dei dati, in<br>conformità con il regolamento generale sulla<br>protezione dei dati (GDPR). * **Trasparenza:**  Il<br>regolamento prevede un livello di trasparenza<br>pubblica delle informazioni sul registro<br>dell'Unione e sull'EUTL, pur mantenendo la<br>riservatezza delle informazioni sensibili.   In<br>sintesi, il Regolamento Delegato (UE) 2019/1122<br>mira a migliorare l'efficienza, la trasparenza e<br>la sicurezza del registro dell'Unione, garantendo<br>l'integrità del sistema EU ETS e la conformità<br>alle normative in materia di strumenti finanziari<br>e protezione dei dati.  Il regolamento entra in<br>vigore il 20° giorno dopo la pubblicazione nella<br>Gazzetta ufficiale dell'Unione europea e si<br>applica dal 1° gennaio 2021, con alcune eccezioni. |
| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This is a long and complex document, but here's a<br>summary of the key information from Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980:  **Purpose:**<br>This regulation supplements Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 on prospectuses for securities offered<br>to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market.  It specifies the format,<br>content, scrutiny, and approval process for<br>prospectuses, and repeals Commission Regulation<br>(EC) No 809/2004.  It aims to increase<br>transparency for investors and harmonize<br>prospectus standards across the EU.  **Key<br>Aspects:**  * **Prospectus Structure:**  The<br>regulation details the required content and order<br>of information within prospectuses,<br>differentiating based on issuer type (e.g., SMEs,<br>frequent issuers), security type (equity, non-<br>equity, asset-backed), and offer type (primary,<br>secondary).  It allows for single-document or<br>separate-document prospectuses (registration<br>document and securities note).  The format is<br>flexible for universal registration documents used<br>annually.  Base prospectuses and final terms are<br>also defined, specifying information to be<br>included in each.  An "overview" section can<br>replace a summary, but can only be called a<br>"summary" if it meets all summary requirements.  *<br>**Information Requirements:**  Detailed annexes<br>specify the minimum information to be included in<br>registration documents and securities notes for<br>various security types.  These requirements vary<br>in comprehensiveness based on the type of investor<br>(retail vs. qualified).  Additional information is<br>required for issuers with complex financial<br>histories, significant financial commitments, or<br>specialized business activities (Annex 29 lists<br>examples of specialist issuers).  Specific<br>requirements are outlined for secondary issuances,<br>closed-end collective investment undertakings,<br>depository receipts, and securities issued by<br>third-country authorities.  Information on<br>underlying assets for derivative securities and<br>asset-backed securities needs detailed disclosure.<br>* **EU Growth Prospectus:**  Simplified rules are<br>provided for EU Growth prospectuses, aimed at<br>reducing the burden on SMEs. A standardized format<br>and reduced information requirements are<br>established, with flexibility allowed within<br>sections.  A specific summary is required with a<br>maximum length of six A4 pages (potentially<br>extended under certain circumstances).  *<br>**Scrutiny and Approval:**  The regulation<br>establishes criteria for competent authorities to<br>scrutinize prospectuses for completeness,<br>comprehensibility, and consistency. It allows for<br>a proportionate approach, including lighter<br>scrutiny for substantially similar prospectuses or<br>those incorporating already-approved information.<br>All submissions must be in searchable electronic<br>format.  Multiple drafts may be submitted, with<br>marked-up versions showing changes.  *<br>**Definitions:**  Key terms like "asset-backed<br>securities," "profit forecast," and "significant<br>gross change" are defined.  * **Repeal:**<br>Commission Regulation (EC) No 809/2004 is<br>repealed.  * **Entry into Force:** The regulation<br>entered into force on the twentieth day following<br>its publication in the Official Journal of the<br>European Union (June 21, 2019) and applied from<br>July 21, 2019.   The regulation is highly detailed<br>and technical, with numerous annexes providing<br>specific information requirements.  This summary<br>highlights the key principles and structural<br>elements; referring to the full text is necessary<br>for the complete and precise details. |

of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy? It aims to create a single market<br>for UWB systems while mitigating potential<br>interference with existing services.  Key aspects<br>include:  * **Harmonization:** The decision<br>establishes harmonized technical conditions for<br>UWB equipment across the EU, addressing issues<br>raised in a CEPT report (CEPT Report 69).  This<br>includes more neutral descriptions of material<br>sensing devices and allowing generic UWB<br>conditions for such applications.  * **Frequency<br>Bands & Power Limits:**  The Annex specifies<br>maximum mean power spectral density (e.i.r.p.) and<br>maximum peak power (e.i.r.p.) limits across<br>various frequency ranges for different UWB<br>applications (generic UWB, location tracking<br>systems (LT1), UWB in motor/railway vehicles,<br>onboard aircraft, and material sensing devices –<br>both contact and non-contact based). These limits<br>vary significantly depending on the frequency band<br>and the specific application.  Specific mitigation<br>techniques (e.g., Low Duty Cycle (LDC), Detect and<br>Avoid (DAA), Transmit Power Control (TPC),<br>trigger-before-transmit) are also defined and<br>required in certain frequency bands and<br>applications to minimize interference.<br>Alternative mitigation techniques are allowed if<br>they provide equivalent protection.  *<br>**Deployment:** Member States must, within six<br>months, make radio spectrum available for UWB<br>equipment meeting the Annex's conditions.  This is<br>on a non-interference, non-protected basis,<br>primarily for indoor use and mobile applications<br>(vehicles). Outdoor fixed installations are<br>generally prohibited, except under specific<br>conditions and mitigation strategies.  *<br>**Monitoring:** Member States are required to<br>monitor UWB usage and report findings to the<br>Commission.  * **Repeal:** Decision 2007/131/EC is<br>repealed.  The decision extensively details<br>technical requirements, including power limits and<br>specific mitigation techniques for various UWB<br>applications and frequency bands.  It emphasizes<br>the need to balance the benefits of UWB technology<br>with the protection of existing radio services.<br>The use of alternative mitigation techniques<br>meeting equivalent performance standards is<br>explicitly permitted. |
| english | Union registry for emissions trading system<br>allowances Union registry for emissions trading<br>system allowances SUMMARY OF: Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122 on the functioning of the Union<br>registry WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?<br>It aims to guarantee accurate accounting for all<br>allowances issued under the European Union (EU)<br>emissions trading system. KEY POINTS EU registry<br>The EU registry is a single, centralised online<br>database run by the European Commission that holds<br>accounts for operators of facilities such as power<br>stations and airline operators. It covers all<br>countries taking part in the EU greenhouse gas<br>emissions trading scheme (EU ETS), set up by<br>Directive 2003/87/EC, which aims to reduce<br>emissions in a cost-effective manner as part of<br>the EU’s policy to tackle climate change. The<br>registry records: facilities covered by the<br>directive in each EU Member State and any free<br>allowances allocated to those facilities;accounts<br>of companies or individuals with such<br>allowances;transfers of allowances performed by<br>account holders;verified annual CO2 emissions of<br>facilities and airline operators;the annual<br>reconciliation of allowances and verified<br>emissions. Phase IV This regulation sets out the<br>general, operational and maintenance requirements<br>for the EU registry for phase IV of the EU ETS<br>from 2021 to 2030. It replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013 (see summary), which covered phase III<br>(2013–2020) of the EU ETS. Main elements The<br>regulation covers a number of aspects, including<br>the following. The registries system, which is<br>operated and maintained by a central<br>administrator. The regulation introduces a EU<br>transaction log (EUTL), which automatically<br>checks, records and authorises all transactions<br>between accounts in the registry. It replaces the<br>Community independent transaction log from phase<br>II. The status and administration of accounts. The<br>regulation simplifies rules on account management<br>with the aim of reducing the burden on national<br>administrators. Specific rules for the EU ETS<br>registry covering issues such as: verified<br>emissions and compliance;transactions, including<br>rules on the execution of transfers and the<br>creation, allocation and transfer of<br>allowances;improving links between the EU ETS and<br>other ETS schemes where a linking agreement was<br>concluded (e.g. the Swiss ETS – see summary).<br>Technical rules and requirements for the registry<br>and EU transaction log, including national<br>helpdesks for account holders and representatives.<br>Repeal It repeals and replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013. The latter continues to apply until 31<br>December 2025 to all operations in relation to the<br>2013–2020 trading period and to the Kyoto accounts<br>until the true-up (the additional period for the<br>completion of commitments) of the second<br>commitment period of the Kyoto Protocol in 2023.<br>FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLY?<br>It has applied since 1 January 2021. BACKGROUND<br>For further information, see: EU registry<br>(European Commission). MAIN DOCUMENT<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 of<br>12 March 2019 supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>of the European Parliament and of the Council as<br>regards the functioning of the Union Registry (OJ<br>L 177, 2.7.2019, pp. 3–62). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>RELATED DOCUMENTS              Commission<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 of 2 May 2013<br>establishing a Union Registry pursuant to<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council, Decisions No 280/2004/EC and<br>No 406/2009/EC of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council and repealing Commission Regulations<br>(EU) No 920/2010 and No 1193/2011 (OJ L 122,<br>3.5.2013, pp. 1–59). See consolidated version.<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 13 October 2003 establishing<br>a scheme for greenhouse gas emission allowance<br>trading within the Community and amending Council<br>Directive 96/61/EC (OJ L 275, 25.10.2003, pp.<br>32–46). See consolidated version. last update<br>11.01.2022 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122, supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>regarding the functioning of the Union Registry<br>for the EU Emissions Trading System (EU ETS).  It<br>outlines rules for the Union Registry (a<br>standardized electronic database for EU ETS<br>allowances) and the European Union Transaction Log<br>(EUTL).  The regulation updates the registry's<br>functionalities to accommodate changes introduced<br>by Directive (EU) 2018/410, which aims to enhance<br>cost-effective emission reductions and low-carbon<br>investments.  **Key Changes and Provisions:**  *<br>**New Trading Period (2021 onwards):** The<br>regulation adapts the registry for the new EU ETS<br>period, including allowances with an indication of<br>their creation period (visible only to account<br>holders when necessary).  Restrictions on<br>allowance surrender ensure allowances can only be<br>used for emissions from the first year of their<br>ten-year issuance period.  International credits<br>are no longer usable from 2021 (except for<br>completing operations related to the 2013-2020<br>period).  * **Alignment with Financial Market<br>Legislation:**  The regulation aligns the Union<br>Registry with Directive 2014/65/EU (Markets in<br>Financial Instruments Directive) by requiring<br>International Securities Identification Numbers<br>(ISIN codes) for emission allowances.  *<br>**Auctioning Process:** Amendments improve<br>alignment of auction processes with Directive<br>98/26/EC (Settlement Finality Directive).  *<br>**Fungibility and Transaction Finality:**<br>Allowances are explicitly defined as fungible and<br>dematerialized, with transactions becoming final<br>and irrevocable upon completion (subject to<br>exceptions for error or fraud).  Good-faith<br>acquisition of allowances is protected.  * **Roles<br>and Responsibilities:**  Clearly defines the roles<br>of the central administrator (operates and<br>maintains the Union Registry and EUTL), national<br>administrators (manage accounts within their<br>Member State), and competent authorities (oversee<br>compliance).  * **Account Management:** Detailed<br>rules cover account opening (including<br>requirements for information and verification),<br>updating, closure, and suspension of access.<br>Procedures for authorized representatives are also<br>specified.  A "trusted account list" simplifies<br>transfers between certain accounts.  * **Verified<br>Emissions and Compliance:** Specifies processes<br>for submitting, verifying, and recording emissions<br>data, including the calculation of compliance<br>status figures.  * **Transactions:**  Outlines<br>rules for various transactions (transfers,<br>allocation, auctioning, surrender, deletion),<br>including the execution timing and potential<br>reversal of transactions in case of errors (within<br>specific timeframes and conditions).  * **Linking<br>with Other Emissions Trading Systems:**  The<br>regulation adapts the Union Registry to<br>accommodate linking agreements with other<br>emissions trading systems.  * **Data Protection:**<br>Addresses data protection requirements under<br>Regulation (EU) 2016/679 (GDPR) and Regulation<br>(EU) 2018/1725, specifying record-keeping and<br>confidentiality provisions.  Joint control of data<br>by the Commission and national administrators is<br>established.  * **Technical Requirements:** Sets<br>out technical requirements for the Union Registry<br>and EUTL, including availability, security,<br>authentication, automated checks, and data<br>reconciliation processes.  Specific reporting<br>requirements are also defined.  * **Transitional<br>Provisions:**  Addresses the continued use of<br>accounts and allowances under the old Regulation<br>(EU) No 389/2013 until specific deadlines, with<br>provisions for handling Kyoto units.  *<br>**Repeal:** Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 is<br>repealed from January 1, 2021, except for<br>operations related to the 2013-2020 trading<br>period.   In essence, this regulation<br>significantly overhauls the Union Registry,<br>modernizing its operations, improving its<br>security, and aligning it with both environmental<br>and financial regulatory frameworks to support the<br>EU ETS's effectiveness. |
| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979 of<br>14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council with regard to regulatory technical<br>standards on key financial information in the<br>summary of a prospectus, the publication and<br>classification of prospectuses, advertisements for<br>securities, supplements to a prospectus, and the<br>notification portal, and repealing Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) No 382/2014 and<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/301 (OJ<br>L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 1–25). See consolidated<br>version. Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980 of 14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council as regards the format, content,<br>scrutiny and approval of the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004 (OJ L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 26–176). See<br>consolidated version. Commission Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 of 16 December 2020<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 of the<br>European Parliament and of the Council as regards<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division (OJ L 106,<br>26.3.2021, pp. 32–46). RELATED DOCUMENTS<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/337 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 16 February 2021<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>EU Recovery prospectus and targeted adjustments<br>for financial intermediaries and Directive<br>2004/109/EC as regards the use of the single<br>electronic reporting format for annual financial<br>reports, to support the recovery from the COVID-19<br>crisis (OJ L 68, 26.2.2021, pp. 1–13). Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This document is the text of COMMISSION DELEGATED<br>REGULATION (EU) 2019/980 of 14 March 2019.  This<br>regulation supplements Regulation (EU) 2017/1129<br>concerning the format, content, scrutiny, and<br>approval of prospectuses for securities offered<br>publicly or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market.  It repeals Commission Regulation (EC) No<br>809/2004.  **Key Aspects of the Regulation:**  *<br>**Prospectus Requirements:** The regulation<br>details specific information requirements for<br>various types of prospectuses,  differentiating<br>based on issuer type (e.g., SMEs, third-country<br>entities), security type (equity vs. non-equity,<br>including asset-backed securities and depository<br>receipts), and offer type (primary vs. secondary).<br>It allows for simplified disclosure in secondary<br>issuances and for EU Growth prospectuses (designed<br>to reduce burden on SMEs).  The regulation<br>emphasizes investor protection and transparency,<br>requiring clear statements regarding competent<br>authority approval and the inclusion of risk<br>factors.  * **Prospectus Format:** The regulation<br>specifies the format of prospectuses (single or<br>multiple documents), base prospectuses, and final<br>terms, including the order of information<br>disclosure.  More flexibility is granted to<br>issuers of universal registration documents<br>published annually.  It clarifies the use of<br>summaries and overview sections, preventing<br>misleading use of the term "summary."  *<br>**Scrutiny and Approval:** Harmonized standards<br>for scrutinizing prospectuses are established,<br>focusing on completeness, comprehensibility, and<br>consistency.  Competent authorities can consider<br>additional criteria for investor protection and a<br>proportionate approach is encouraged (lighter<br>scrutiny for similar prospectuses or when<br>information is already reviewed).  Electronic<br>submission of documents in searchable format is<br>mandated, along with marked-up versions showing<br>changes between drafts.  * **Specific Annexes:**<br>The regulation includes numerous annexes detailing<br>specific information requirements for various<br>types of registration documents and securities<br>notes, covering aspects like persons responsible,<br>risk factors, financial information, corporate<br>governance, offer terms, and guarantees.  Separate<br>annexes detail requirements for EU Growth<br>prospectuses and specific summary formats.  A list<br>of specialist issuers (property, mineral,<br>investment, research, start-up, shipping<br>companies) is also included, indicating that these<br>may be subject to more stringent requirements.<br>**Effective Date:** The regulation entered into<br>force on the twentieth day following its<br>publication in the Official Journal of the<br>European Union and applied from 21 July 2019. |
| english | Short range devices, RLAN (WiFi), Internet of<br>Things, ultra-wide band (UWB) equipment and<br>Intelligent Transport Systems (ITS) Short range<br>devices, RLAN (WiFi), Internet of Things, equipment<br>Decision 2010/368/EU amending Decision 2006/771/EC<br>on harmonisation of the radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices Decision 2009/381/EC amending<br>Decision 2006/771/EC on harmonisation of the radio<br>spectrum for use by short-range devices Decision<br>2007/90/EC amending Decision 2005/513/EC on the<br>harmonised use of radio spectrum in the 5 GHz<br>frequency band for the implementation of Wireless<br>Access Systems including Radio Local Area Networks<br>(WAS/RLANs) Decision 2008/411/EC on the<br>harmonisation of the 3 400-3 800 MHz frequency<br>band for terrestrial systems capable of providing<br>electronic communications services Decision<br>2005/513/EC on the harmonised use of radio<br>spectrum in the 5 GHz frequency band for the<br>implementation of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy?
