Council Directive 91/287/EEC of 3 June<br>1991 on the frequency band to be designated for<br>the coordinated introduction of digital European<br>cordless telecommunications (DECT) into the<br>Community (OJ L 144, 8.6.1991, pp. 45-46) RELATED<br>DOCUMENTS              Directive (EU) 2018/1972 of<br>the European Parliament and of the Council of 11<br>December 2018 establishing the European Electronic<br>Communications Code (Recast) (OJ L 321,<br>17.12.2018, pp. 36-214) See consolidated version.<br>Decision No 676/2002/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 7 March 2002on a regulatory<br>framework for radio spectrum policy in the<br>European Community (Radio Spectrum Decision) (OJ L<br>108, 24.4.2002, pp. 1-6) last update 12.11.2020 | This Commission Implementing Decision (EU)<br>2019/785 harmonizes radio spectrum use for ultra-<br>wideband (UWB) technology in the European Union,<br>repealing Decision 2007/131/EC.  It aims to create<br>a single market for UWB systems while mitigating<br>potential interference with existing services like<br>radio astronomy.  The decision mandates Member<br>States, within six months, to allocate radio<br>spectrum for UWB equipment (meeting specified<br>conditions in the Annex) on a non-interference,<br>non-protected basis.  This applies to indoor use<br>and outdoor use not involving fixed installations<br>or antennas, and is extended to motor and railway<br>vehicles.  Member States must monitor usage and<br>report to the Commission.  The Annex details<br>technical requirements for UWB usage, categorized<br>into:  * **Generic UWB Usage:** Specifies maximum<br>mean power spectral density (e.i.r.p.) and peak<br>power (e.i.r.p.) limits across various frequency<br>bands (from below 1.6 GHz to above 10.6 GHz), with<br>options for mitigation techniques like Low Duty<br>Cycle (LDC) and Detect and Avoid (DAA).  *<br>**Location Tracking Systems Type 1 (LT1):**<br>Similar to generic UWB but with slightly different<br>power limits.  * **UWB Devices in Motor and<br>Railway Vehicles:**  Includes stricter power<br>limits and mandatory trigger-before-transmit<br>mitigation in certain bands (3.8-4.2 GHz and 6-8.5<br>GHz) to reduce interference.  LDC, DAA, or<br>Transmit Power Control (TPC) techniques are<br>options.  * **UWB Onboard Aircraft:** Defines<br>power limits and necessary mitigation techniques<br>in various frequency bands, including specific<br>protections for Fixed Satellite Service (FSS) and<br>Meteorological Satellite (MetSat) bands.  *<br>**Material Sensing Devices (Contact and Non-<br>Contact):**  Specifies different power limits for<br>contact and non-contact devices, including options<br>for LBT mechanism and limitations on duty cycle,<br>with restrictions on fixed outdoor installations<br>in certain frequency ranges.  These devices must<br>also minimize emissions.  The decision allows for<br>alternative mitigation techniques if they provide<br>equivalent spectrum protection and comply with<br>Directive 2014/53/EU.  The specific details of<br>these techniques, including references to relevant<br>ETSI standards, are included in the Annex's<br>footnotes. |
| english | Union registry for emissions trading system<br>allowances Union registry for emissions trading<br>system allowances SUMMARY OF: Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122 on the functioning of the Union<br>registry WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?<br>It aims to guarantee accurate accounting for all<br>allowances issued under the European Union (EU)<br>emissions trading system. KEY POINTS EU registry<br>The EU registry is a single, centralised online<br>database run by the European Commission that holds<br>accounts for operators of facilities such as power<br>stations and airline operators. It covers all<br>countries taking part in the EU greenhouse gas<br>emissions trading scheme (EU ETS), set up by<br>Directive 2003/87/EC, which aims to reduce<br>emissions in a cost-effective manner as part of<br>the EU’s policy to tackle climate change. The<br>registry records: facilities covered by the<br>directive in each EU Member State and any free<br>allowances allocated to those facilities;accounts<br>of companies or individuals with such<br>allowances;transfers of allowances performed by<br>account holders;verified annual CO2 emissions of<br>facilities and airline operators;the annual<br>reconciliation of allowances and verified<br>emissions. Phase IV This regulation sets out the<br>general, operational and maintenance requirements<br>for the EU registry for phase IV of the EU ETS<br>from 2021 to 2030. It replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013 (see summary), which covered phase III<br>(2013–2020) of the EU ETS. Main elements The<br>regulation covers a number of aspects, including<br>the following. The registries system, which is<br>operated and maintained by a central<br>administrator. The regulation introduces a EU<br>transaction log (EUTL), which automatically<br>checks, records and authorises all transactions<br>between accounts in the registry. It replaces the<br>Community independent transaction log from phase<br>II. The status and administration of accounts. The<br>regulation simplifies rules on account management<br>with the aim of reducing the burden on national<br>administrators. Specific rules for the EU ETS<br>registry covering issues such as: verified<br>emissions and compliance;transactions, including<br>rules on the execution of transfers and the<br>creation, allocation and transfer of<br>allowances;improving links between the EU ETS and<br>other ETS schemes where a linking agreement was<br>concluded (e.g. the Swiss ETS – see summary).<br>Technical rules and requirements for the registry<br>and EU transaction log, including national<br>helpdesks for account holders and representatives.<br>Repeal It repeals and replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013. The latter continues to apply until 31<br>December 2025 to all operations in relation to the<br>2013–2020 trading period and to the Kyoto accounts<br>until the true-up (the additional period for the<br>completion of commitments) of the second<br>commitment period of the Kyoto Protocol in 2023.<br>FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLY?<br>It has applied since 1 January 2021. BACKGROUND<br>For further information, see: EU registry<br>(European Commission). MAIN DOCUMENT<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 of<br>12 March 2019 supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>of the European Parliament and of the Council as<br>regards the functioning of the Union Registry (OJ<br>L 177, 2.7.2019, pp. 3–62). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>RELATED DOCUMENTS              Commission<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 of 2 May 2013<br>establishing a Union Registry pursuant to<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council, Decisions No 280/2004/EC and<br>No 406/2009/EC of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council and repealing Commission Regulations<br>(EU) No 920/2010 and No 1193/2011 (OJ L 122,<br>3.5.2013, pp. 1–59). See consolidated version.<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 13 October 2003 establishing<br>a scheme for greenhouse gas emission allowance<br>trading within the Community and amending Council<br>Directive 96/61/EC (OJ L 275, 25.10.2003, pp.<br>32–46). See consolidated version. last update<br>11.01.2022 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122, supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>regarding the functioning of the Union Registry<br>for the EU Emissions Trading System (EU ETS).  It<br>details the rules for operating and maintaining<br>the Union Registry and the European Union<br>Transaction Log (EUTL),  effective January 1,<br>2021, with some exceptions.  **Key changes and<br>provisions:**  * **New EU ETS Trading Period (2021<br>onwards):**  The regulation adapts the registry to<br>the new period, including marking allowances with<br>their creation decade (visible only to account<br>holders when necessary for distinguishing<br>allowances from different phases) and restricting<br>allowance surrender to emissions from the first<br>year of their issuance.  International credits are<br>no longer permitted from 2021 (though existing<br>operations related to the 2013-2020 period<br>continue under the previous regulation).  *<br>**Classification of Allowances as Financial<br>Instruments:**  The rules align with financial<br>market legislation (Directives 2014/65/EU and<br>98/26/EC), requiring the display of ISIN codes for<br>allowances in the registry.  Auction processes are<br>better aligned with Directive 98/26/EC.  *<br>**Fungibility and Irrevocability of Allowances:**<br>Allowances are defined as fungible and<br>dematerialized. Transactions are generally final<br>and irrevocable upon completion, protecting good-<br>faith purchasers.  Reversals are possible only<br>under specific circumstances and within defined<br>timeframes, primarily for unintentional errors.  *<br>**Roles and Responsibilities:**  The roles of the<br>central administrator (managing the registry and<br>EUTL) and national administrators (managing<br>national accounts and user contact) are clearly<br>defined.  * **Account Management:**  Detailed<br>procedures for account opening, updating<br>(including authorized representatives), and<br>closure are outlined, including requirements for<br>information provision and verification.  Specific<br>provisions address operator and aircraft operator<br>accounts, including suspension of access under<br>certain conditions (e.g., suspected fraud, non-<br>compliance).  A "trusted account list" facilitates<br>faster transactions.  * **Verified Emissions and<br>Compliance:** Procedures for submitting and<br>verifying emissions data are specified, along with<br>the calculation of compliance status figures.<br>Failure to submit verified emissions results in<br>account blocking.  * **Transactions and<br>Allowances:**  Rules governing allowance transfers<br>(including auctions and free allocation),<br>surrender, and deletion are detailed, emphasizing<br>the automated checking and recording of<br>transactions by the EUTL.  * **Linking with Other<br>Emissions Trading Systems:** The regulation<br>addresses the operationalization of linking<br>agreements, including allowance transfers and<br>account management.  * **Data Protection and<br>Confidentiality:**  The regulation addresses data<br>protection compliance (Regulations (EU) 2016/679<br>and 2018/1725), outlining record-keeping<br>requirements and confidentiality provisions,<br>specifying the permitted release of data to law<br>enforcement, supervisory and other relevant<br>authorities.  * **Transitional Provisions:**  The<br>regulation details the continued application of<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 for operations related<br>to the 2013-2020 period and amends that regulation<br>accordingly.  It also outlines procedures for<br>handling existing Kyoto units.  * **Technical<br>Requirements:**  The regulation sets out technical<br>requirements for the Union Registry and the EUTL,<br>including availability, security, authentication,<br>and automated checking mechanisms.  Data exchange<br>and technical specifications are to be provided by<br>the Commission.  The regulation aims to streamline<br>the EU ETS registry while maintaining<br>environmental integrity and security.  Member<br>States are responsible for implementing the<br>necessary national provisions. |
| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979 of<br>14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council with regard to regulatory technical<br>standards on key financial information in the<br>summary of a prospectus, the publication and<br>classification of prospectuses, advertisements for<br>securities, supplements to a prospectus, and the<br>notification portal, and repealing Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) No 382/2014 and<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/301 (OJ<br>L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 1–25). See consolidated<br>version. Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980 of 14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council as regards the format, content,<br>scrutiny and approval of the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004 (OJ L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 26–176). See<br>consolidated version. Commission Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 of 16 December 2020<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 of the<br>European Parliament and of the Council as regards<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division (OJ L 106,<br>26.3.2021, pp. 32–46). RELATED DOCUMENTS<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/337 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 16 February 2021<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>EU Recovery prospectus and targeted adjustments<br>for financial intermediaries and Directive<br>2004/109/EC as regards the use of the single<br>electronic reporting format for annual financial<br>reports, to support the recovery from the COVID-19<br>crisis (OJ L 68, 26.2.2021, pp. 1–13). Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This is Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980, adopted on March 14, 2019, and effective<br>July 21, 2019.  It supplements Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 concerning prospectuses for securities<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market, repealing Regulation (EC) No<br>809/2004.  The regulation details requirements for<br>the **format, content, scrutiny, and approval of<br>prospectuses**, differentiating requirements based<br>on issuer type, security type, and offer type.<br>Key aspects include:  * **Prospectus Content:**<br>Specifies minimum information for various<br>registration documents (equity securities,<br>universal registration documents, secondary<br>issuances, closed-end collective investment<br>undertakings, depository receipts,<br>retail/wholesale non-equity securities, asset-<br>backed securities, and securities from third-<br>country entities).  It also dictates minimum<br>information for securities notes corresponding to<br>each registration document type.  Additional<br>information requirements are outlined for issuers<br>with complex financial histories or significant<br>financial commitments, securities convertible into<br>shares, securities linked to underlying assets,<br>asset-backed securities, and guarantees.  *<br>**Prospectus Format:**  Defines the structure of<br>prospectuses (single document vs. separate<br>registration document and securities note), base<br>prospectuses, and final terms, including the order<br>of information disclosure.  More flexibility is<br>granted to issuers using annual universal<br>registration documents.  It clarifies the use of<br>the term "summary" and requires a clear<br>explanation of any deviations from the prescribed<br>order of information.  Specific formatting rules<br>are detailed for EU Growth prospectuses, including<br>its summary.  * **Scrutiny and Approval:**<br>Establishes criteria for scrutinizing the<br>completeness, comprehensibility, and consistency<br>of prospectuses.  It allows competent authorities<br>to consider additional criteria for investor<br>protection and to apply a proportionate approach,<br>particularly for similar prospectuses or those<br>incorporating information by reference.  The<br>regulation mandates electronic submission of<br>prospectuses in searchable format, including<br>marked-up and clean versions of subsequent drafts.<br>It specifies the documents to be submitted at<br>different stages of the approval process and the<br>timelines for acknowledgment and notification of<br>decisions.  The regulation also addresses the<br>scrutiny of prospectuses from "specialist issuers"<br>(property, mineral, investment, research, start-<br>up, and shipping companies).  * **EU Growth<br>Prospectus:**  Sets out specific content<br>requirements for EU Growth registration documents<br>and securities notes for both equity and non-<br>equity securities, including a detailed format and<br>length restrictions for its summary.  In short,<br>the regulation aims to harmonize prospectus<br>requirements across the EU, enhance investor<br>protection, and improve the efficiency of the<br>prospectus approval process.  It replaces the<br>outdated Regulation (EC) No 809/2004. |

terrestrial systems capable of providing<br>electronic communications services Decision<br>2005/513/EC on the harmonised use of radio<br>spectrum in the 5 GHz frequency band for the<br>implementation of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy? Council Directive 91/287/EEC of 3 June<br>1991 on the frequency band to be designated for<br>the coordinated introduction of digital European<br>cordless telecommunications (DECT) into the<br>Community (OJ L 144, 8.6.1991, pp. 45-46) RELATED<br>DOCUMENTS              Directive (EU) 2018/1972 of<br>the European Parliament and of the Council of 11<br>December 2018 establishing the European Electronic<br>Communications Code (Recast) (OJ L 321,<br>17.12.2018, pp. 36-214) See consolidated version.<br>Decision No 676/2002/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 7 March 2002on a regulatory<br>framework for radio spectrum policy in the<br>European Community (Radio Spectrum Decision) (OJ L<br>108, 24.4.2002, pp. 1-6) last update 12.11.2020 | This document is Commission Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2019/785, dated May 14, 2019, harmonizing<br>radio spectrum use for ultra-wideband (UWB)<br>technology within the European Union.  It repeals<br>Decision 2007/131/EC.  **Purpose:** To harmonize<br>technical conditions for the availability and<br>efficient use of radio spectrum by UWB equipment,<br>ensuring efficient spectrum usage while coexisting<br>with other users.  This includes avoiding harmful<br>interference with existing radiocommunication<br>services, including radio astronomy, earth<br>exploration satellite, and space research systems.<br>**Key Definitions:** The decision defines key<br>terms, including "equipment using ultra-wideband<br>technology" (short-range radiocommunication with a<br>frequency range wider than 50 MHz), "non-<br>interference and non-protected basis," "indoors,"<br>"motor vehicle," "railway vehicle," and various<br>power density measurements (e.i.r.p., maximum mean<br>power spectral density, peak power, total power<br>spectral density).  It also defines "onboard<br>aircraft" and "LT1" (systems for general location<br>tracking).  **Spectrum Allocation:** Member States<br>must, within six months, designate radio spectrum<br>for UWB equipment (on a non-interference, non-<br>protected basis) meeting the Annex's conditions.<br>This applies to indoor use and outdoor use *not*<br>involving fixed installations, infrastructure, or<br>antennas.  UWB use is also permitted in motor and<br>railway vehicles.  **Monitoring and Reporting:**<br>Member States are required to monitor UWB band<br>usage and report findings to the Commission to<br>ensure continued relevance of the conditions.<br>**Technical Requirements (Annex):** The Annex<br>details extensive technical requirements, varying<br>by frequency range and UWB application type:  *<br>**Generic UWB Usage:** Specifies maximum mean and<br>peak power spectral densities (e.i.r.p.) across<br>various frequency bands (from below 1.6 GHz to<br>above 10.6 GHz). * **Location Tracking Systems<br>Type 1 (LT1):** Similar to generic UWB, but with<br>slightly different power limits. * **UWB Devices<br>in Motor and Railway Vehicles:**  Includes<br>stricter power limits and mandates the use of<br>mitigation techniques like Low Duty Cycle (LDC),<br>Detect and Avoid (DAA), or Transmit Power Control<br>(TPC) in certain frequency bands, along with an<br>exterior limit.  Trigger-before-transmit<br>mitigation is required for vehicular access<br>systems in specific bands. * **UWB Onboard<br>Aircraft:**  Specifies power limits and mitigation<br>techniques, including notch filters in certain<br>frequency ranges to protect Fixed Satellite<br>Service (FSS) and Meteorological Satellite<br>(MetSat). * **Material Sensing Devices:**  Divided<br>into contact-based and non-contact-based types,<br>each with its own set of stricter power limits and<br>requirements for mitigation techniques (LDC, DAA,<br>LBT) and some frequency ranges with no fixed<br>outdoor installations permitted.  A Listen Before<br>Talk (LBT) mechanism is required for certain<br>frequency ranges.  The Annex also allows for<br>alternative mitigation techniques if they provide<br>equivalent performance and spectrum protection,<br>and comply with Directive 2014/53/EU.  References<br>to relevant ETSI standards are provided for many<br>mitigation techniques.  **Repeal:** Decision<br>2007/131/EC is repealed. |
| english | Union registry for emissions trading system<br>allowances Union registry for emissions trading<br>system allowances SUMMARY OF: Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/1122 on the functioning of the Union<br>registry WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?<br>It aims to guarantee accurate accounting for all<br>allowances issued under the European Union (EU)<br>emissions trading system. KEY POINTS EU registry<br>The EU registry is a single, centralised online<br>database run by the European Commission that holds<br>accounts for operators of facilities such as power<br>stations and airline operators. It covers all<br>countries taking part in the EU greenhouse gas<br>emissions trading scheme (EU ETS), set up by<br>Directive 2003/87/EC, which aims to reduce<br>emissions in a cost-effective manner as part of<br>the EU’s policy to tackle climate change. The<br>registry records: facilities covered by the<br>directive in each EU Member State and any free<br>allowances allocated to those facilities;accounts<br>of companies or individuals with such<br>allowances;transfers of allowances performed by<br>account holders;verified annual CO2 emissions of<br>facilities and airline operators;the annual<br>reconciliation of allowances and verified<br>emissions. Phase IV This regulation sets out the<br>general, operational and maintenance requirements<br>for the EU registry for phase IV of the EU ETS<br>from 2021 to 2030. It replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013 (see summary), which covered phase III<br>(2013–2020) of the EU ETS. Main elements The<br>regulation covers a number of aspects, including<br>the following. The registries system, which is<br>operated and maintained by a central<br>administrator. The regulation introduces a EU<br>transaction log (EUTL), which automatically<br>checks, records and authorises all transactions<br>between accounts in the registry. It replaces the<br>Community independent transaction log from phase<br>II. The status and administration of accounts. The<br>regulation simplifies rules on account management<br>with the aim of reducing the burden on national<br>administrators. Specific rules for the EU ETS<br>registry covering issues such as: verified<br>emissions and compliance;transactions, including<br>rules on the execution of transfers and the<br>creation, allocation and transfer of<br>allowances;improving links between the EU ETS and<br>other ETS schemes where a linking agreement was<br>concluded (e.g. the Swiss ETS – see summary).<br>Technical rules and requirements for the registry<br>and EU transaction log, including national<br>helpdesks for account holders and representatives.<br>Repeal It repeals and replaces Regulation (EU) No<br>389/2013. The latter continues to apply until 31<br>December 2025 to all operations in relation to the<br>2013–2020 trading period and to the Kyoto accounts<br>until the true-up (the additional period for the<br>completion of commitments) of the second<br>commitment period of the Kyoto Protocol in 2023.<br>FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULATION APPLY?<br>It has applied since 1 January 2021. BACKGROUND<br>For further information, see: EU registry<br>(European Commission). MAIN DOCUMENT<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 of<br>12 March 2019 supplementing Directive 2003/87/EC<br>of the European Parliament and of the Council as<br>regards the functioning of the Union Registry (OJ<br>L 177, 2.7.2019, pp. 3–62). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2019/1122 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>RELATED DOCUMENTS              Commission<br>Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 of 2 May 2013<br>establishing a Union Registry pursuant to<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council, Decisions No 280/2004/EC and<br>No 406/2009/EC of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council and repealing Commission Regulations<br>(EU) No 920/2010 and No 1193/2011 (OJ L 122,<br>3.5.2013, pp. 1–59). See consolidated version.<br>Directive 2003/87/EC of the European Parliament<br>and of the Council of 13 October 2003 establishing<br>a scheme for greenhouse gas emission allowance<br>trading within the Community and amending Council<br>Directive 96/61/EC (OJ L 275, 25.10.2003, pp.<br>32–46). See consolidated version. last update<br>11.01.2022 | This is a lengthy and complex document, but here's<br>a summary of Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/1122, which supplements Directive 2003/87/EC<br>regarding the EU Emissions Trading System (EU ETS)<br>Union Registry:  **Purpose:** The regulation<br>establishes operational and maintenance<br>requirements for the Union Registry (a<br>standardized electronic database for EU ETS<br>allowances) and the European Union Transaction Log<br>(EUTL).  It updates the system to reflect changes<br>introduced by Directive (EU) 2018/410, aligning it<br>with financial market legislation (e.g.,<br>Directive 2014/65/EU on markets in financial<br>instruments) and preparing for the EU ETS's fourth<br>trading period (starting 2021).  **Key Changes and<br>Provisions:**  * **New Trading Period (2021<br>onwards):**  The registry will now indicate the<br>ten-year period in which allowances were created<br>(visible only to account holders when necessary to<br>distinguish allowances from different periods).<br>Restrictions are implemented to ensure allowances<br>can only be used for emissions within the first<br>year of their issuance period.  International<br>credits (under the Kyoto Protocol) are no longer<br>permitted from 2021, though existing transactions<br>will be processed under previous regulations until<br>2026.  * **Financial Instrument Classification:**<br>The regulation adapts to the classification of<br>emission allowances as financial instruments,<br>requiring the display of ISIN codes in the<br>registry and aligning processes with market abuse<br>and settlement finality directives.  * **Account<br>Management:**  Detailed rules are set for account<br>opening (operator holding accounts, aircraft<br>operator holding accounts, trading accounts),<br>account status (open, blocked, closure pending,<br>closed, excluded), authorized representatives, and<br>account updates.  Stricter verification procedures<br>are introduced to prevent fraud and money<br>laundering.  * **Transactions:**  The regulation<br>specifies procedures for allowance transfers,<br>execution times, and transaction reversals (with<br>strict limits and conditions). It emphasizes the<br>fungible and dematerialized nature of allowances,<br>protecting good-faith purchasers.  * **Emissions<br>and Compliance:** Rules for submitting verified<br>emissions data, calculating compliance status<br>figures, and blocking accounts for non-compliance<br>are defined.  * **Allocation:** Procedures for<br>free allocation of allowances to stationary<br>installations and aircraft operators are<br>clarified, including the handling of national<br>allocation tables and corrections for over-<br>allocation.  * **Auctions:**  The regulation<br>outlines the transfer of allowances to auction<br>accounts, the management of auction tables in the<br>EUTL, and the handling of any changes or necessary<br>amendments.  * **Linking with other ETS:**<br>Provisions are included for linking the EU ETS<br>with other emissions trading systems, including<br>account creation, transaction processes, and<br>conditions for suspending the link.  * **Data<br>Protection:** The regulation emphasizes compliance<br>with data protection regulations (GDPR, Regulation<br>(EU) 2018/1725), defining roles and<br>responsibilities of data controllers (Commission<br>and national administrators) and outlining record-<br>keeping and data retention requirements.  *<br>**Confidentiality:**  Strict rules on<br>confidentiality of registry data are established,<br>with limited exceptions for law enforcement and<br>regulatory bodies.  * **Technical Requirements:**<br>Detailed technical requirements for the Union<br>Registry and EUTL are outlined, covering<br>availability, security, authentication, automated<br>checks, and error handling.  * **Transitional<br>Provisions:**  The regulation addresses the<br>transition from the previous system (Regulation<br>(EU) No 389/2013), specifying the continued use of<br>certain accounts and the handling of existing<br>Kyoto units.  Regulation (EU) No 389/2013 is<br>repealed from 1 January 2021, except for<br>operations related to the 2013-2020 trading period<br>(until 1 January 2026).   In short, this<br>regulation significantly overhauls the EU ETS<br>Union Registry, enhancing its security,<br>efficiency, and alignment with both environmental<br>and financial market regulations.  It aims to<br>streamline operations while maintaining the<br>environmental integrity of the EU ETS. |
| english | Prospectus to be published when securities are<br>offered to the public or admitted to trading on a<br>regulated market Prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market SUMMARY OF:<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979<br>supplementing Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on<br>regulatory technical standards on key financial<br>information in the summary of a prospectus, the<br>publication and classification of prospectuses,<br>advertisements for securities, supplements to a<br>prospectus, and the notification portal Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/980 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on format, content, scrutiny and<br>approval of the prospectus to be published when<br>securities are offered to the public or admitted<br>to trading on a regulated market Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/528 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 on the minimum information content<br>of the document to be published for a prospectus<br>exemption in connection with a takeover by means<br>of an exchange offer, a merger or a division WHAT<br>IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION? Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 (the prospectus regulation), as<br>supplemented by Delegated Regulations (EU)<br>2019/979, 2019/980 and 2019/528, aims to help<br>companies, including small and medium-sized<br>enterprises (SMEs), access different forms of<br>finance in the European Union (EU). It does so by<br>simplifying and streamlining the rules and<br>procedures for drawing up, approving and<br>distributing the prospectus* they publish when<br>offering securities* to the public or admitting<br>securities to trading on a regulated market. The<br>legislation reduces costly and burdensome red tape<br>for companies and enables investors to make the<br>right investment decision by providing<br>comprehensible, easy to analyse and concise<br>information. KEY POINTS                The<br>regulation: removes the need for a prospectus for<br>any offer of securities to the public, including<br>crowdfunding (raising money from a large group of<br>people, often via the internet) projects, below €1<br>million (previously the limit was €100,000);<br>allows EU Member States to be exempt from the need<br>for a prospectus for offers of securities to the<br>public of up to €8 million, provided that they do<br>not require notification (a ‘passport’); sets out<br>rules to curb the tendency to overload<br>prospectuses with generic risk factors;<br>strengthens supervisory convergence by harmonising<br>scrutiny and approval of prospectuses (including<br>the applicable timelines) throughout the EU;<br>enables companies that frequently issue securities<br>to use the universal registration document to<br>secure fast-track approval from supervisors within<br>5 days; introduces a European online database,<br>operated free of charge by the European Securities<br>and Markets Authority (ESMA), containing all<br>prospectuses approved in the European Economic<br>Area. The regulation requires a prospectus to<br>enable an investor to make an informed decision.<br>It must include: assets, liabilities, profits,<br>losses, financial position and prospects for the<br>issuer and any guarantor; rights attached to the<br>securities; reasons for issuing the securities and<br>their impact on the issuer; a clear and accurate<br>seven-page summary (except for the admission to<br>trading of non-equity securities only targeting<br>qualified investors), which provides: an<br>introduction with warnings that the investor could<br>lose all or part of the invested capital,key<br>information on the securities, including the type<br>and class of securities and the rights attached to<br>the securities,information about the issuer,a<br>brief description of the nature and scope of a<br>guarantee. The regulation establishes a<br>standardised and simplified EU growth prospectus<br>for: SMEs, defined in Directive 2014/65/EU (the<br>MiFID II directive) (see summary) as companies<br>which meet at least two of the following three<br>criteria: an average number of employees during<br>the financial year of less than 250,a total<br>balance sheet not exceeding €43 million,an annual<br>net turnover not exceeding €50 million; issuers,<br>other than SMEs, whose securities are traded or to<br>be traded on an SME growth market (a market that<br>offers access to capital for SMEs), with an<br>average market capitalisation (market value of the<br>company’s shares) of below €500 million; offerors<br>of securities issued by issuers referred to in the<br>two previous points; non-listed companies (not<br>listed on any stock market) which offer securities<br>to the public of less than €20 million in any<br>given 12 months, provided that they have fewer<br>than 500 employees; issuers, other than SMEs, that<br>offer shares to the public and at the same time<br>seek admission of those shares to trading on an<br>SME growth market, provided that: such issuers<br>have no shares already admitted to trading on an<br>SME growth market,the combined value of the final<br>offer price (or, if not available, the maximum<br>price) and the total number of shares outstanding<br>immediately after the share offer to the public is<br>less than €200 million. The abovementioned<br>companies can benefit from this tailored<br>prospectus provided that they have no securities<br>admitted to trading on a regulated market. The<br>regulation provides for a simplified prospectus<br>for companies listed for at least 18 months on a<br>regulated market or an SME growth market and<br>wishing to issue additional shares or raise debt<br>(secondary issuance). The regulation harmonises<br>the minimum information content of the document to<br>be published for a prospectus exemption in<br>connection with a takeover by means of an exchange<br>offer, a merger or a division. Amending<br>regulations Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 seeks to<br>promote the use of SME growth markets by reducing<br>formalities and administrative burdens on SMEs in<br>terms of disclosure obligations and a simplified<br>prospectus. Regulation (EU) 2020/1503 introduces a<br>prospectus exemption for offers of securities to<br>the public made by crowdfunding service providers<br>that do not exceed the threshold of €5 million in<br>accordance with the conditions specified in that<br>regulation. Regulation (EU) 2021/337 introduces a<br>new ‘EU recovery prospectus’ to help companies<br>recover from the COVID-19 crisis. This shorter<br>prospectus, with a maximum length of 30 pages plus<br>a two-page summary, makes it easier for companies<br>to raise capital to meet their funding needs,<br>while ensuring adequate information is provided to<br>investors. The recovery prospectus will be<br>available for capital increases of up to 150% of<br>outstanding capital within a period of 12 months<br>and applies until the end of 2022. Delegated acts<br>The European Commission has adopted the following<br>acts. Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980 laying<br>down details of the precise content and format of<br>the prospectus, as well as concerning the scrutiny<br>and approval of the prospectus. Delegated<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/979 laying down details of<br>the key financial information in the summary of<br>the prospectus, the publication and classification<br>of the prospectus, the advertisement for the<br>securities and the supplement to a prospectus.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1273 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/980.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2020/1272 amending and<br>correcting Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 setting out the<br>minimum information content of the document to be<br>published for a prospectus exemption in connection<br>with a takeover by means of an exchange offer, a<br>merger or a division. Report The Commission is<br>required to report on the application of the<br>legislation before 21 July 2022. FROM WHEN DO THE<br>REGULATIONS APPLY? Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and<br>Delegated Regulations (EU) 2019/979 and (EU)<br>2019/980 have applied since 21 July 2019.<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) 2021/528 has applied<br>since 15 April 2021. BACKGROUND Directive<br>2003/71/EC was designed to make it easier for<br>companies to raise capital throughout the EU on<br>the basis of approval from just one national<br>supervisor. This gave a ‘passport’ for<br>prospectuses containing cross-border offers.<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129, which repeals and<br>replaces Directive 2003/71/EEC, addresses the<br>areas of legal uncertainty and unjustified<br>administrative burdens which had emerged over<br>time. It is considered a major milestone towards a<br>European capital markets union. For further<br>information, see: Securities prospectus (European<br>Commission) Prospectus (European Securities and<br>Markets Authority). KEY TERMS<br>Prospectus. A legal document describing a<br>company’s main line of business, finances and<br>shareholding structure. Potential investors use it<br>to decide whether to buy the securities a company<br>offers. Securities. Shares, bonds and derivatives.<br>MAIN DOCUMENTS              Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council of 14 June 2017 on the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Directive 2003/71/EC (OJ L<br>168, 30.6.2017, pp. 12–82). Successive amendments<br>to Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 have been<br>incorporated in the original text. This<br>consolidated version is of documentary value only.<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2019/979 of<br>14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation (EU)<br>2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of the<br>Council with regard to regulatory technical<br>standards on key financial information in the<br>summary of a prospectus, the publication and<br>classification of prospectuses, advertisements for<br>securities, supplements to a prospectus, and the<br>notification portal, and repealing Commission<br>Delegated Regulation (EU) No 382/2014 and<br>Commission Delegated Regulation (EU) 2016/301 (OJ<br>L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 1–25). See consolidated<br>version. Commission Delegated Regulation (EU)<br>2019/980 of 14 March 2019 supplementing Regulation<br>(EU) 2017/1129 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council as regards the format, content,<br>scrutiny and approval of the prospectus to be<br>published when securities are offered to the<br>public or admitted to trading on a regulated<br>market, and repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004 (OJ L 166, 21.6.2019, pp. 26–176). See<br>consolidated version. RELATED DOCUMENTS<br>Regulation (EU) 2021/337 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 16 February 2021<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>EU Recovery prospectus and targeted adjustments<br>for financial intermediaries and Directive<br>2004/109/EC as regards the use of the single<br>electronic reporting format for annual financial<br>reports, to support the recovery from the COVID-19<br>crisis (OJ L 68, 26.2.2021, pp. 1–13). Regulation<br>(EU) 2020/1503 of the European Parliament and of<br>the Council of 7 October 2020 on European<br>crowdfunding service providers for business, and<br>amending Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 and Directive<br>(EU) 2019/1937 (OJ L 347, 20.10.2020, pp. 1–49).<br>Regulation (EU) 2019/2115 of the European<br>Parliament and of the Council of 27 November 2019<br>amending Directive 2014/65/EU and Regulations (EU)<br>No 596/2014 and (EU) 2017/1129 as regards the<br>promotion of the use of SME growth markets (OJ L<br>320, 11.12.2019, pp. 1–10). last update 22.11.2021 | This document is Commission Delegated Regulation<br>(EU) 2019/980 of 14 March 2019, supplementing<br>Regulation (EU) 2017/1129 on prospectuses for<br>securities offered to the public or admitted to<br>trading on a regulated market.  It specifies the<br>format, content, scrutiny, and approval of<br>prospectuses, repealing Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004.  The regulation aims to increase<br>transparency and investor protection.  **Key<br>aspects covered:**  * **Definitions:**  Clarifies<br>terms like "asset-backed securities," "equivalent<br>third country market," "profit estimate," and<br>"significant gross change."  * **Prospectus<br>Content:**  Details minimum information<br>requirements for various registration documents<br>and securities notes, categorized by security type<br>(equity, non-equity, secondary issuances,<br>depository receipts, asset-backed securities,<br>etc.), issuer type (including third-country<br>issuers), and investor type (retail vs.<br>qualified).  It mandates additional information<br>for issuers with complex financial histories or<br>significant financial commitments, securities<br>convertible into shares, and asset-backed<br>securities.  Specific information requirements are<br>tailored to different types of securities and<br>investors.  * **Prospectus Format:** Specifies the<br>order of information for prospectuses (single or<br>multiple documents), base prospectuses, and final<br>terms.  It allows for flexibility in the order of<br>information within the universal registration<br>document and EU Growth prospectus, but requires a<br>cross-reference list if the order deviates from<br>the Annexes.  Clarifies the use of "summary" and<br>"overview" sections.  * **EU Growth Prospectus:**<br>Simplifies the requirements for SMEs, laying down<br>a fixed order for information presentation, but<br>allowing flexibility within sections.  It<br>specifies detailed requirements for the<br>registration document and securities note,<br>differentiating between equity and non-equity<br>securities.  It also details requirements for the<br>specific summary, including its maximum length.  *<br>**Scrutiny and Approval:** Sets out criteria for<br>scrutinizing the completeness, comprehensibility,<br>and consistency of prospectuses.  It allows<br>competent authorities to use a proportionate<br>approach, considering additional criteria where<br>necessary and conducting lighter scrutiny for<br>similar prospectuses or information already<br>reviewed.  It mandates electronic submission of<br>documents in searchable format, including marked-<br>up and clean versions of revised drafts.  It<br>specifies the documents required at different<br>stages of the approval process and the timelines<br>for acknowledgment and decision notification.  It<br>also addresses the process for specialist issuers.<br>* **Repeal:**  Repeals Commission Regulation (EC)<br>No 809/2004.  * **Entry into force:** The<br>regulation entered into force on the twentieth day<br>following its publication in the Official Journal<br>of the European Union (June 21, 2019) and applied<br>from July 21, 2019.   The regulation includes<br>numerous annexes detailing the specific<br>information required for each type of prospectus<br>and its components.  These annexes are extensively<br>detailed within the main text but are too long to<br>fully reproduce in this summary. |

of wireless access systems<br>including radio local area networks (WAS/RLANs)<br>Directive 91/287/EEC on the frequency band to be<br>designated for the coordinated introduction of<br>digital European cordless telecommunications<br>(DECT) into the Community WHAT ARE THE AIMS OF THE<br>DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS? The implementing<br>decisions mostly concern harmonisation, while<br>others deal with specific frequency bands for<br>specific purposes, in addition to limits on signal<br>strength and harmful interference where<br>applicable. EU countries are responsible for radio<br>spectrum management, and the amendments reflect<br>how European and international harmonisation and<br>technical agreements have evolved. The ‘DECT’<br>directive designates the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency<br>band for digital cordless communications by 1<br>January 1992 and obliges EU countries to bring<br>into force the necessary national laws,<br>regulations and administrative rules. KEY POINTS<br>The decisions The implementing decisions cover<br>radio equipment devices that are operated through<br>general authorisation or on an unlicensed or<br>shared basis by end-users. This includes radio<br>local access network devices (wi-fi) devices which<br>have shown massive growth in demand for radio<br>spectrum, as acknowledged in the 2018 European<br>Electronic Communications Code. Many of these acts<br>are harmonisation decisions. Others deal with<br>frequency bands for different purposes, such as a<br>huge variety of short range devices, Internet of<br>Things (IoT) equipment, ultra-wide band equipment,<br>alarms, door openers, medical implants,<br>intelligent transport systems, radio frequency<br>identification devices (RFID), radio<br>determination, ground probing, and new types of<br>machine-to-machine devices, as well as equipment<br>for programme making and special events (PMSE)<br>such as wireless video links or microphones and<br>digital cordless telephones. A further general<br>authorisation band relates to vehicle safety, in<br>particular to the operation of Intelligent<br>Transport Systems (ITS). The various implementing<br>decisions cover the following radio spectrum, in<br>addition to limits on signal strength and harmful<br>interference where applicable: the 5 GHz frequency<br>band (5 150-5 350 MHz and 5 470-5 725 MHz) for<br>wireless access systems, including radio local<br>area networks (WAS/RLANs — wi-fi broadband); the 3<br>400-3 800 MHz frequency band for terrestrial<br>systems for ‘fixed, nomadic and mobile electronic<br>communications networks’; the 5 875-5 935 MHz<br>frequency band for safety-related applications of<br>Intelligent Transport Systems; the radio spectrum<br>for use by short-range devices; the 24 GHz range<br>radio spectrum band for the time-limited use by<br>automotive short-range radar equipment; radio<br>spectrum use by wireless audio programme-making<br>and special events equipment; the 2 010-2 025 MHz<br>frequency band for portable or mobile wireless<br>video links and cordless cameras used for<br>programme making and special events; the 900 MHz<br>and 1 800 MHz frequency bands for terrestrial<br>systems capable of providing electronic<br>communications services in relation to the<br>Internet of Things; radio spectrum for use by<br>short-range devices within the 874-876 and 915-921<br>MHz frequency bands; radio spectrum for equipment<br>using ultra-wideband technology, such as vehicle<br>and aircraft location tracking. Directive<br>91/287/EEC The directive obliges EU countries to<br>designate the 1 880-1 900 MHz frequency band for<br>digital cordless communications by 1 January 1992.<br>FROM WHEN DO THE DIRECTIVE AND DECISIONS APPLY?<br>Legislation Application date Implementing Decision<br>(EU) 2020/1426 8 October 2020 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2019/785 16 May 2019 Implementing<br>Decision (EU) 2018/1538 12 October 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2018/637 23 April 2018<br>Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/2077 13 November<br>2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2017/1483 10<br>August 2017 Implementing Decision (EU) 2016/339 9<br>March 2016 Implementing Decision 2014/641/EU 2<br>September 2014 Implementing Decision 2013/752/EU<br>12 December 2013 Implementing Decision 2011/829/EU<br>9 December 2011 Implementing Decision 2011/485/EU<br>1 August 2011 Decision 2010/368/EU 1 July 2010<br>Decision 2009/381/EC 14 May 2009 Decision<br>2007/90/EC 12 February 2007 Decision 2008/411/EC<br>21 May 2008 Decision 2005/513/EC 11 July 2005<br>Directive 91/287/EEC 5 June 1991 BACKGROUND<br>For more information, see: What is Radio Spectrum<br>Policy?
